	 prisoner.
		-Silver Maw seemed alarmed that we had one of them here, but Blood Stained Wind approved,
		 apparently on the same page as me, saying she could be a valuable source of information.
	-After walking upstairs, the lunars spent some time examining the paintings in the parlor, while
	 Libak, Blade, and I stepped aside to discuss how we should continue.
		-Mostly, I was unsure if we should make introductions amongst the other Exalt-types without
		 settling the matter of the oath.
			-Ultimately, we decided the oath must first go forward.
		-The subject of Larquen Quen also came up, with Blade asking if anyone knew who this was,
		 he being that one that had betrayed his past incarnation. . .
			-Blade had apparently missed Libak and my exchange on this subject before, so I was
			 rather cagey and did not admit to being him reborn.
			-Blade spoke at some length of the undying magnitude of Quen's sin, though some oblique
			 cajoling on my part got him to admit that the combination of his and Quen's death both
			 may have settled the matter.
			-In the course of this, Pip also disclosed some knowledge of Quen, and a commitment to
			 _not_ murdering him (a nice change!).
	-With our plan settled, we left the lunars in the parlor, to go administer the oath.
		-Gaman assented to the oath.
	-With that done, Libak disclosed the news of our new shapeshifting visitors.
		-Gaman's face showed alarm at the mention of the lunars, but she held her tongue.
	-Returning to the parlor, Two-Faced Raven was staring at the image of Meherrin, while Blood
	 Stained Wind pointedly looked everywhere _but_ the portrait of Quen.
		-I preformed the introductions, and we set about dicussing our next course of action.
		-In the course of this, Libak mentioned that the storm was now gone. Two-Faced Raven had
		 apparently dispelled it, suggesting a sorcerous origin for it.
			-That certainly increases our options.
		-We also discussed the business that brought the lunars here.
			-Silver Maw's was already fairly clear, and indeed he'd come seeking out "his" Morning
			 Star.
				-The discussion veered into some awkward and alarming sexual tension between the two
				 of them for a bit.
			-Two-Faced Raven also seemed to be here seeking Blade, saying, somewhat cryptically, that
			 he was "weak", for seeking the trappings of this manse, claiming that they could show
			 him he had no need for such things.
			-Blood Stained Wind remained silent through this, and so I addressed her directly, asking
			 what brought _her_ here.
				-Me speaking to her seemed to cause her visible discomfort, but she kept glancing at
				 Silent Onyx, eventually addressing him as "her Vaznia", and complaining that he'd
				 given away her wedding gift, gesturing at the Amulet of Shadowwalking that Libak
				 currently carried.
				-Libak nervously returned the amulet to Onyx, saying something about having "just
				 borrowed it."
				-I think that gives us a strong sense of what her motivation is here, then.
		-We decided to return to our exploration of the manse, as we still sought the hearthstone.
			-Blood Stained Wind expressed some amusement at the thought of "Vaznia" robbing tombs,
			 a thing she claimed Vaznia would once have thought beneath her.
			-Two-Faced Raven said she'd remain and keep watch over "this thing", in reference to our
			 dragonborn prisoner (ally?). Silver Maw also opted to remain, after a brief exchange
			 with Golden Blade.
	-We went back to the (false) tomb of Kal Bax, to resume what we were working on when Silent Onyx
	 was injured.
		-After some hemming and hawing, Golden Blade volunteered to be our gas-canary, and we lowered
		 him into the tomb, to see if the gas that had attacked Onyx's skin had dissipated.
		-Blood Stained Wind also followed him in, after shifting into the form of a hummingbird,
		 though one that retained distinctly snake-like scales around the eyes.
		-They reported no sign of the gas below, so Silent Onyx slid down the rope to join them.
		-Carefully examining the strangely fresh stonework he'd noticed earlier, Onyx found that,
		 rather than stones, it was a grid of buttons.
		-Following traces of repeated fingerprints on _some_ of the stones, Onyx was able to press
		 the correct pattern, allowing the wall to swing inwards, revealing a passage.
		-Inside, a long hallway, supported by pillars and decorated with glazed tiles of many colors,
		 led to another doorway.
		-Taking the lead, Onyx approached the door, only to hear a click as he stepped up to it.
		-He thankfully managed to dodge what turned out to be a razor-thin wire of orichalcum, studded
		 with blue crystals to form a sawblade-like texture.
			-Perhaps a thing worth coming back to, given the valuable orichalcum.
		-More carefully now, he examined the door before proceeding, then boldly tried the knob.
		-Inside was a chamber containing nothing but another door, this time emblazoned with a golden
		 sunburst.
			-I recognized it as a common form of magical door, one the exalted often used for vaults
			 and the like where they wished to keep mortals out. Most commonly, they simply required
			 that essence be fed in to open.
			-I indeed began to feed essence into it, mote by mote.
			-Onyx, meanwhile, had his attention caught by a portion of the wall. Scraping away at it,
			 he found the "stone" to be a facade, concealing a small door, just large enough for an
			 adult to crawl through.
			-I abandoned my attempts at what I now suspected was a mere distraction, as Blade crawled
			 through the revealed door.
		-It led to a pillared chamber, featuring two levers, one at the center of six sunbursts.
			-I took a look inside myself, but neither of use could make much sense of what we saw,
			 though something about the construction of the room felt. . . off to me.
			-Blood Stained Wind confirmed my impression, suggesting that it was the pillars that
			 were wrong, missing two in the center the pattern called for.
			-Onyx found that the pillars were threaded through with fine wire, connected to the
			 sunburst door in a way suggesting the room would collapse were it opened.
			-The wires provided the crucial clue, though, as, tracing them, they carefully avoided
			 one door-sized section of wall. Searching the area carefully, Onyx found a lever hidden
			 near the base of the wall and, flipping it, indeed opened a hidden door there.
		-That led to yet another hallway, terminating in a door inside an alcove.
			-Onyx approached the door, only for the floor to again click at his step, leading to the
			 floor falling away, and him with it.
				-He was able to avoid rocks beneath or the debris falling with him, as he plunged
				 into freezing water.
				-Thankfully, he was able to climb out of the dunk shaft.
			-I came to join him in the room above after his fall and shout, while he searched
			 the room further, finding many more pit traps like the first.
			-He also carefully examined the door, finding no traps, just a lock, and so picked
			 the lock and went through.
		-I followed him into the next room after hearing a voice call out in Old Realm, saying,
		 "One of us speak the truth. The other only lies."
			-Inside, there were three faces on the walls, one smiling, one neutral, and one
			 frowning, it's mouth opening onto a stairway. As I entered, the neutral face
			 repeated the statement, and again, when Pip joined us.
			-Onyx asked aloud, "Which way to the hearthroom?"
				-The smiling face responded, "This way!" opening it's mouth to reveal another
				 stairway leading down.
			-Pip asked the other, frowning face, "Is what your brother said true?"
				-"Yes, it is."
			-I then asked the central, neutral face, "What of you? Are you involved in the game
			 or are you simply the referee, which only yielded a repeat of its message.
			-Pip then asked, of both masks leading to passages, "Do you speak The rivertongue?"
				-The both of them responded in the Rivertongue, the smiling one saying "No," and
				 the frowning one saying, "Yes!"
			-Shit, that's _both_ of them lying at one point or another.
			-After a bit more back and forth, Pip asked them if they were _both_ liars, and they
			 both responded, "No," both lying (speech in the Rivertongue now enabling the use of
			 Judge's Ear by those who have it, as they do not speak Old Realm).
			-It would seem both _can_ lie, and, thinking back, the riddle only specified that
			 one always _lied_, and that the other _does_ speak the truth, and may not be
			 _obligated_ to.
			-With that realization, we quickly determined the one frowning always lied, and was
			 thus, paradoxically, our best source of truth.
			-We were then able to get it to quickly reveal to us, through lies, that it contained
			 (what it considered, at least, to be) the correct passage, and we sent Silent Onyx
			 down it.
		-That led down to another door, opening into a chamber with five more doors.
			-One door was open, leading to a room covered in scorch marks.
				-Perhaps the triggered remains of yet another trap?
			-While Onyx was off down that passage, Blood Stained Wind spoke up: "Do you remember
			 the pact we made?"
				-We were all once members of The Black Nadir Concordant. All save Silent Onyx. . .
				-Blood Stained Wind found the mirror while we broke open the tombs of The Neverborn
				 retrieving it from sunken Oceanus.
				-Vaznia sought the mirror, meaning to prove our crimes against the Solar deliberative
				 and we, sworn to keep each other's secrets, kept it from her.
					-She was unaware, at very least, of Blood Stained Wind's membership in the
					 Concordant.
				-Blood Stained Wind recommended that we kill Silent Onyx, before he discovered the
				 secret of her, and our, betrayal.
				-"What, though, was the mirror?", we asked her. "Why did Vaznia want it?"
					-"Larquen told me some things about it. He said it could twist the essence of a
					 Solar that looked into it, and that such things would enable greater mastery of
					 the dead."
						-Hmm. . . that reminded me of the deathknights,  
					-She also mentioned that the mirror was a shard of obsidian glass, and one that
					 shed cold to the extent that she was forced to carry it wrapped in many layers
					 of cloth.
					-Well, that did not sound like the mirror we found, though I felt compelled to
					 check, showing it to Blood Stained Wind.
					-She confirmed that it was not the mirror she spoke of, but said that she _did_
					 recognize it, and was surprised Vaznia had kept it.
						-It was the work of mortal hands, but a sentimental object, the mirror
						 through which Vaznia had once watched her as she brushed Vaznia's hair.
				-We were less than enthused about murdering Onyx, and worked to talk Blood Stained
				 Wind out of it.
					-She eventually relented on this score, but still seemed uneasy, and asked that
					 we keep her secret, and the secret of this mirror, from Onyx.
					-On the latter, I had some concerns. What if he found, and _looked into_ the
					 mirror?
					-We decided it was best to at least inform him of the mirrors danger, though
					 we could certainly keep silent about our part in it's presence here.
		-We joined Silent Onyx in the chamber down the hallway.
			-He said he believed he'd found the way forward, and we in turn warned him not to look
			 into any cold obsidian mirrors, lest it "twist our essences".
				-He was thankfully incurious about how we learned this.
		-Following the path Onyx had found, we found a chamber containing a ramshackle door set into
		 a marble archway and a strange white-jade plate, 10' across, and studded with runes and
		 blue crystal spiked caltrop shapes.
			-The door seemed constructed from debris from the manse above, and featured a keyhole.
			-The plate, meanwhile, had a key and swordhilt with a shaft of bamboo growing from it,
			 lying near the center of the plate.
				-I recognized it as a species of magnet, but knew no more.
				-Onyx claimed he could likely open the door without the key, but we wanted that
				 sword. . .
				-As such, Golden Blade stepped onto the plate, and all of us suddenly felt a tug
				 towards it.
				-Most of us managed to find a handhold to grab onto, but Libak was sucked towards the
				 plate and it's caltrops.
				-He was nearly impaled on one of the caltrops, but his anima flared as he used a
				 charm, and the spike failed to pierce his now oak-hard skin.
				-A moment later, the magnet's force reversed, and all of us were suddenly being
				 pushed towards the ceiling.
				-This time, though, all of us managed to hold on.
				-Finally, magnet's force relaxed, Onyx opened the lock on the door, the rest of us
				 quickly following him.
					-Libak even managed to grab the bamboo-bladed sword.
		-This chamber featured a large porcelain mask who, at our arrival opened it's eyes.
			-"Halt!", it said, first in Old Realm and then repeating it in many languages. "Speak the
			 password or die!", it continued, again repeating it in each language, then finally
			 shouting in all at once, "You have 30 seconds!"
			-After a stressful 28 seconds, Pip recovered a timely memory of her past incarnation,
			 speaking the password and yielding a "Greetings, honored ones." from the mask, and an
			 open door.
			-We passed through it into the next door, and left off the session there.


9/27/21:
	-That last door led to yet another hallway, with a door at the end.
	-Bloodstained Wind and Silent Onyx scouted ahead, checking for more traps, and eventually opened
	 the door.
		-It led to an altar, a small golden dais, standing before a statue of The Unconquered Sun
		 that was depicted holding up the ceiling.
			-The plaque said, "Through me, you are exalted."
			-I having approached close enough to read the plaque, the statue's eyes lit with golden
			 solar essence, writhing like flames.
			-As I stepped into the room, the writhing essence flared, and a bolt shot forward at me.
			-I thankfully dodged it, in no small part because it shot at my hip, or seemingly at the
			 paired jade blades hanging there.
			-Well, this is a place of The Unconquered Sun, and those the tools of the Terrestrials.
			-We decided to shed such items for the moment, stashing them in the cache egg.
				-I kept, though, both my bracers and the phylactery. They being Orichalcum, I
				 reasoned they may be allowed.
			-Sure enough, stepping again, tentatively, into the room, I was spared another blast.
		-We saw no exit from the room, though.
			-A careful examination, though, revealed scratches along one wall.
			-They looked like the marks of a bladed weapon, but went far too high on the wall for
			 most to reach.
			-We examined the ceiling above, and Silent Onyx was able to spot the outline of a
			 tightly fitted trapdoor.
	-I boosted Onyx up and he was easily able to push the door out of the way, leading to a narrow,
	 roughly cut tunnel, which he climbed into.
		-He eventually shouted that he'd reached a grid made of up of ominous looking beams of
		 essence.
		-I shouted up that the Amulet of Shadowwalking could likely take him past it, and indeed it
		 seemed to.
		-After most of an hour, without hearing from Silent Onyx, we heard a great crash, from
		 somewhere else within the manse.
		-At that, I had Blade boost me up, and I climbed down the tunnel.
			-It was indeed as Onyx described it, the grid of beams still there.
			-I saw no way to disable or bypass it myself, and told the others it looked as Onyx
			 had said.
			-Libak turned to Bloodstained Wind, and asked _her_ if she could perhaps make it through,
			 shapeshifter that she is.
			-She flew up to examine it with me. As she did so, her eyes changed, from lizard,
			 to bird, to mammal.
				-As she did so, her forehead began to glow with a silver-y light in the form of a
				 crescent moon.
			-After a moment, she said that she _could_ pass through the grid, but that we had missed
			 something, and she began to scratch at the plaster of the nearby wall with her newly
			 formed claws, slowly revealing a plastered over doorway.
			-I called for the others, lowering a rope for them, and we passed through the doorway,
			 down a tunnel that neatly circumvented the grid.
			-From there, we seemingly followed in Onyx's footsteps, through a series of strange rooms,
			 until we reached a section of hallway where the walls moved, slamming into each other
			 and then retracting, again and again.
			-I thought I could make it through, but was not sure we all could.
			-Golden Blade volunteered his, well, blade, and jammed it into the mechanism behind one
			 wall as it attempted to retract.
				-Using the blade as a lever, and pulling with all his strength, he broke part of the
				 wall free from the piston it connected too, releasing a great gout of steam.
				-After that, the wall moved no more, and we were through.
	-Just through there, we found Silent Onyx, himself having recently clawed his way through some
	 fallen stone blocking his passage back.
		-"Come," he said, "I've found more coffins to loot."
		-He led us to a set of four small coffins, that he began checking for traps.
		-None found, we opened them, finding some empty, but in one we found a strange looking mask,
		 double-faced and grisly, part of it broken.
		-Golden Blade froze at the sight of the mask.
			-When he finally spoke, he said that he had seen this mask before, worn by The Mask of
			 Winter, as he conquered Thorns.
		-I, too, recognized the mask: https://discord.com/channels/@me/772891797726822481/892218728081657866
			-"you have a small memory of making this mask, using meherrin's skin... the last thing
			 you made before being thrown into that hole by Ozandus Pal...
			 not an artifact, just a grim trophy of your most savored kill"
		-The chamber also held a mask on one wall, which now began to speak (seemingly on a timer).
			-It named us trespassers, but said that the children of The Unconquered Sun were merciful
			 (seemingly not recognizing us as among them) demanding we swear an oath to leave the
			 manse and tell no one of it.
			-Onyx, though, in breaking and clawing through the blockage in the passage behind us, had
			 already removed it's leverage. . .
		-Onyx also showed me a bit of Old Realm he'd recorded, scrawled in one of the earlier rooms.
			-"He was too crazy. We had to kill him. I took that stupid mask he made, broke his legs,
			 threw him in a hole, and covered him."
			-I (unwisely?) read that aloud as I went. . .
		-Given this grisly thing, what do we know about ghosts?
			-They're attracted to the blood of the living, and are attached to things they were
			 passionate about in life, including sometimes pieces of their bodies.
			-Humans have two souls, the hun, the higher soul, and the po, the lower soul. The hun can
			 become a ghost, while the po can rise as a "hungry ghost".
			-In a Shadowland, ghosts are tangible and real, and can even have children, the "ghost
			 blooded".
				-Thorns is now one such Shadowland, and Sijon a particularly famous one.
	-Onyx was heavily taxed getting this far, and suggested we rest a bit, before continuing on.
		-One of the rooms we had passed through featured beds, some bolt hole for the Solars of the
		 manse.
		-We agreed that would be wise, closed the room's doors, and set a watch.
		-My sleep, though, was troubled by dreams.
			-As I slept, I felt cold and, waking, could not move (sleep paralysis).
			-The mask we'd recently recovered tumbled around the bed, rising then into the air, the
			 eyes like vortexes.
			-It spoke: "I will find you. I will make you suffer."
			-I awoke, but knew myself to still be dreaming. I was in one of the bedrooms above,
			 emaciated, and began to crawl from bed, towards the door, only to be stopped by a man
			 with a golden staff, shaped like a tree branch, who grabbed me and began to drag me.
			-I tried to fight him, but could muster little strength, as he dragged me downstairs and
			 threw me into my tomb. The last sight I saw was the slab closing off the light above,
			 though the dream continued, through hours (days?) of scratching at the walls of the
			 tomb. While I scratched, I began to hear voices, voices agreeing I'd been cheated,
			 robbed of what should have been mine. Serve us, they called, and all of it would be
			 mine. . .
		-Libak, upon awakening, told me my First Age incarnation was a dick.
			-I acknowledged that I had become conscious of the same, since arriving here.
			-I asked him, though, why he said that now.
			-It would seemed he dreamed too, of the origin of the mask. . .
			-I acknowledged that I knew too, and offered a sheepish apology.
				-He, thankfully, seemed confident those earlier incarnations were not _us_, and we
				 had a good philosophical debate, confident in the end that we could succeed where
				 they failed.
			-In discussing the matter, a thought occurred to me. Larquen had been _jealous_ of
			 Meherrin, jealous that he had achieved _The Second Circle of Necromancy_. The price
			 The Primordials had demanded of Larquen was service, a price he was unwilling to pay.
				-Did _Meherrin_ pay the same? Does that have something to do with why The Mask of
				 Winters wears _this_ mask? 
	-We then resumed where we left off, sweeping the room with the coffins, and finding another
	 plastered-over door.
		-It was thoroughly locked, like a vault, but, with Onyx's help, we eventually had it open.
		-It led to another hallway, and then eventually to a room with four more doors.
		-We opted to first backtrack to the T-intersection, and check those other two doors,
		 before continuing down this lengthy branch.
	-The first door there we opted to open was marked with an air symbol.
		-Onyx checked the door for traps and, finding none, opened it onto a swirling vortex of blue
		 energy, and a freezing wind.
			-His thin form is not suited to such things and, slamming the door, he came away freezing.
			-Libak was feeling bold, though, and had recently learned Charms to deal with very much
			 this sort of thing, and opted to open the door again himself, as we took shelter around
			 the corner.
			-He could weather it no better, though.
		-That sent us back upstairs, to warm the pair of them in the tubs above.
			-While they soaked, though, I, and Bloodstained Wind to stave off any further attacks,
			 went to go let the Lunars and Terrestrial know we were still alive.
				-They seemed fine, if bored, reporting no attacks or the like.
				-The Terrestrial Dynast requested something to read, and I said I'd see what I could
				 do, though warned her most of the books in the manse had been destroyed.
					-I debated the matter with the others, once back below, but we had nothing that
					 wasn't full of terrible secrets, or just terribly priceless.
	-It took the pair of them several hours to recover, but we eventually returned to the maze,
	 heading back to the T-intersection.
		-We were a bit reluctant to try the remaining door, but Golden Blade was characteristically
		 bold, and reached for the the knob on the door marked with the water symbol.
		-The door would not budge, but he began to cough up sea water, then bits of kelp, and even
		 a fish.
		-Thankfully, and not coincidentally, he's also the one of us best equipped to bull his way
		 through the effects of an attempted drowning, and he survived it without ill-effect.
	-From there, we returned to the five doors in the room in the South.
		-Silent Onyx now did a thorough check of the room, wary as we were of the many "obvious"
		 doors in earlier rooms that proved to be traps.
		-No other doors, or traps, were found, but two of the five doors here showed signs of
		 having been opened. One had bits of stone debris in front of it, while the other had
		 scrapes before it, like things had been dragged into it.
		-Trying the door something had been dragged into, I found a treasure trove.
			-It contained (all in Roll20):
				-A pair of Orichalcum and moonsilver torcs 
				-An instrument
				-A jagged shard of black jade, with a handle wrapped in dingy leather
				-A plain Orichalcum mask.
				-A breastplate.
				-A hookah.
				-A wujong blade, or so I thought. When I looked away, and back, it was now a cutlass.
					-This sounds familiar to me.
					-Yep, it's The Forgotten Blade in Roll20, though, strangely, I seem to be the
					 only one who can consistently recognize it without being attuned to it.
				-A pair of orichalcum hearthstone bracers.
			-They all were arranged, like a ritual altar, around a flat object wrapped in white cloth.
				-Silent Onyx, quite sure what it was, grabbed it, and wrapped it tighter.
				-Libak asked if Onyx thought that was a mirror and, at Onyx's nod, offered his
				 jacket to wrap it further.
					-Onyx mentioned "not being sure how I feel about the memories of my last
					 incarnation", but felt strongly that this was a thing to take great care with.
					-This was all rather out of character for him.
				-Bloodstained Wind, at the sight of it, looked panicked, and looking from Onyx to
				 rest of us and back, she turned into a snake and fled.
					-We made no attempt to stop her or follow, with several of the others convinced
					 she'd soon return with the other Lunars, though I'm less sure of that.
				-We decided the safest place for such a thing would be our Cache egg. We'd trust it
				 to no hands but our own, but also keep it safely (?) Elsewhere.
	-After examining the treasures for a bit, Onyx went to mark the other _used_ door.
		-He sooned called out to me, as the inside was covered in Old Realm writing.
		-It was a messy scrawl, much of it gibberish, but a few repeating lines formed a coherent
		 theme: "I did it! I killed him, but now the voices in the mirror call to me. The only place
		 I'm safe is here!"
		-Venturing further into the twisting, rough-carved room, following the writing, I came to a
		 desicated corpse. It lay beside a long staff, clearly an artifact, and had around it's_
		 neck a hearthstone socketed in an amulet.
		-Clearly, I've found Osandus Pal.
		-As I approached to retrieve the hearthstone, the corpse sat up suddenly, shouting, "No, not
		 you! Anyone but you!", only to tumble to dust afterward, followed by what seemed to be a
		 wind that swept past us, out the way we'd came.
	-Pal's preferences aside, I grabbed the hearthstone, and the amulet it was in, and, with our
	 major goal in hand, immediately set about attuning to it.
		-I can now see through any mirror in the manse.
		-I can also see that the manse's essence flows are being forced into a disharmonic state,
		 causing the level of the hearthstone to fluctuate. This appears to be due to the fact that
		 something has crashed the barriers preventing I Am from accessing every portion of the manse.
		-In fact, from what I can now tell, and despite what it said, I Am seems to very much be
		 fully functional. . .
		-As if in response to this probing of the manse's systems, a voice, seemingly coming from
		 everywhere, began to shout, "No!!! It's mine!"


10/1/21: A First Age Interlude
	-Jeff not being able to make Council of Wyrms, Lesley, Jake, and I played a one-shot thing as
	 our First Age selves.
	-Hmm. . . Larquen's character sheet suggests _his_ Metasorcerous Phylactery works with Necromancy
	 too.
	-Both Morning Star and Larquen are members of The Black Nadir Concordant.
		-Morning Star dispises me, though, like most.
		-Study of The Underworld is strictly forbidden by The Solar Deliberative, but we said
		 fuuuuuccck that, and of course did so.
		-We delved into The Underworld from Sijan.
		-Once there, we entered The Labyrinth, and in it's heart, broke open the tombs of the
		 slain Primordials, and stole the secrets of Necromancy.
	-After that, we met in Denandsor, The Empty City.
		-The city is a showpiece of the Twilight caste, a display of their crafting prowess.
		-Meherrin, Aure Orchester joined us there also.
		-There too were Kal Bax, his apprentice Osandus Pol, Daveg, and Itraxian.
			-The four of them help rule the city.
			-Bax was the one who called us there.
			-He named the other four of us as ones who'd taken the forbidden journey to The
			 Underworld, in the same breath as he admitted interest in making the same journey.
			-He then pulled out a strange puzzle box.
				-Made of strange black ore bound in Orichalcum.
				-Examined with Sorcerer's Sight, the thing is fucking crazy, folded space, necromantic
				 energies, and portals.
				-"Where did you get this?" Morning Star asked. "I made it."
					-"Why?" "Nothing should stand in the way of progress. Certainly not sanity."
				-"What do you intend to do with such a thing?" I asked. "I intend to journey to the
				 heart of The Underwold, stepping through this device."
				-"What do you want there?" Morning Star asked. "I have heard the whispers in the
				 deep caverns, speaking of secrets take to the graves of the slain Primordials."

			 with his box.
	-Nothing happened at first, but then, in the blink of an eye, we were elsewhere.
		-At least, Morning Star and I were. The others were nowhere to be found.
			-Was this a mistake? Or intentional? We both strongly considered the latter. . .
		-We were clearly in The Labyrinth, surrounded by pillars topped in pools of icho.
		-I knew this place as The Pools of Consumption, an area _within_ one of the tombs of
		 The Primordials.
			-The tomb of The Perfect Principal of Consumption.
		-There too is The Palace the Forsaken, at the heart of the tomb, though The Many
		 Mounds lie between us and there.
		-Movement, in The Underworld, is strange, though, a matter of will, and of the wills

			-Spending a Willpower _will_ get you where you're going, but attract The
			 Malevolence.
	-With my guidance, we navigated from there to The Many Mounds, heading to our destination.
		-This area was a biomechanical Giger homage, populated by sickly looking birds, cancer-
		 ridden and missing patches of skin.
		-As we travelled on, we encountered a tall, skinny figure, wrapped entirely in leather,
		 bleeding from the eye holes.
			-I recognized it as Endless Consumption of The Flesh, a component soul of one of The
			 Primordials.
			-Morning Star warned it was ready for a fight, and I fell into my Snake Form, but, as

				-It _is_ ill. _Deeply_. It shows signs of a vast number of vile diseases, and from
				 the essence flows surrounding it, it seemed to be _radiating_ the same.
			-Battle it was, then.
				-It acted first, attempting to infect us with something horrible, though it was
				 warded off by our Resistance charms.
				-Morning Star then swung at it, but missed the quick moving horror.
				-I, though, surged forward, muttering command phrases that turned my skin to
				 bronze and hands to claws, and, with the aid of Supreme Perfection of Martial Arts,
				 ripped it's chest open, to examine it's insides.
				-As I did so, I also employed Ghost Eating Technique, sucking, Marceline's-Dad-like,
				 it's very essence from it.
					-_That_ seemed to put some fear into it's eye-holes.

	-We took advantage of Morning Star's summoned-for-the-battle flying battle armor to take the

					 as well.

	 then took wing.
		-The inside was appointed like a lavish passenger ship.

				-This seeming to be the "machine" he was called to build, and I eagerly encouraged

					-A few moment later, Bax opened his eyes, and then immediately bounced to his

					-He then spoke: "Strange. It asked for the memories of my time spent as a mortal.
					 And now I understand."
						-A price worth paying in my eyes. A price Garn later _would_ pay.

				-At that, Garn hung his head and did not speak.
			-She also, then, took notice of Pip's shortsword, retrieved from the tomb of her past
			 self.
				-"You recognize this blade?" I asked.
				-She asked Pip, "Can you draw it?"
				-As it was drawn, it grows from shortsword to orichalcum daiklaive, with sutras
				 written along it's side, and a name: Sunspeaker.
				-At the sight of it, she screamed, fell backwards, and started crawling back away
				 from the exposed blade.
				-Pip sheathed it and, when she had calme a bit, she spoke: "What you carry is The 
				 Howler in Darkness," she said, "Where was The Silver Prince buried?"
					-Pip recognized the name, she being a native of Nexus. They're a Deathlord.
						-And, then, is her First Age self The Silver Prince?
					-Libak also got a look of disgust on his face, apparently connecting some dots,
					 and spoke, ". . . I think Meherrin may be The Walker in Darkness. I remember
					 making a deal. . ."
					-I then confessed that I suspect Larquen Quen became The Mask of Winters.
					-The deathknight looked shocked, but then asked us if we knew the tale of
					 Princess Magnificent.
						-Those of the circle from Nexus did. She had ruled a Shadowland near here,
						 and had warred on Great Forks.
						-It looked like she might win, but the guardians of Great Forks eventually
						 found something, a connection to her original body, or maybe the weapon that
						 killed her.
						-The lesson was rather clear.
			-She also asked again, "What is to become of me?"
				-Rather than answer her, I asked, "What would you do with you? Were you free? Return
				 to your master?"
				-"I am bound to him. I would, but would go first to The Underworld."
				 "Bound to one or bound to another, huh?"
				 "Under The Mask, I had freedom."
					-Garn, silent for a bit, eventually just walked away.
	-Unloading the ship took a day.
		-At the end of it, we were each given 2 talens of silver, our shares, granting us Resources 5
		 for the rest of the month.
	-The kidnappings continued, now including nobles, merchant families, and other centers of power.
		-The strange thing, though, that has really riled people up, is the fact that The Emissary
		 has not acted against a single person. . .
		-A group called the Tang Zen was at war with another, The Black Syndicate, along with a
		 child gang ("The Crows") and a new-formed gang of Terrestrials ("The Triple Threats").
			-All sorts of trouble is being caused by that, but still The Emissary does not act.
		-Pip's mother also came to see her, thankful for her return.
			-Apparently she'd been barely able to eat, owing to what she has had to pay in protection
			 money to a snakemen gang.
			-Pip is enraged, and intent on doing something about that.
		-I did some drinking with Blade and Hawke's men, to celebrate our success (again, if they
		 knew. . .).
			-The chaos of the city was well evident while we were out.
			-We also heard rumors of the disappearance of the very poor in Nexus too.
				-The guards have been writing it off, but the working class is worried.
				-Some body parts have been found in the water near the docks, and in other waters
				 throughout the city. Could be the work of animals, but rumors abound about some
				 kind of monster.
					-Sightings were rumored in the Firewander district, at night. A big silver mass
					 seen moving across the rooftops, and supposedly in and out of the Wyld-zone
					 there.
			-Much carousing occurred, and we even found ourselves in an underground fighting ring
			 for a bit, to many cheers.
			-Eventually we found our way back to Hawke's compound, where Golden Blade keeps a room.
			-I found a message waiting there for me, from my monks.
				-They asked me to come to the monastery, and, obliquely, suggested I "avoid the
				 usual ways", what I understood to refer to my Wooden Face spell.
		-The next morning, a very angry Libak came in, slamming a piece of paper down on the table.
			-"I can't believe it," he said, "They took my brother."
			 "Who," I asked, "took him?"
			-In response, he gestured at the paper.
				-Reading it, it was a contract between his brother and Ophilis Ses. It's a work
				 contract, but harsh, indentured servitude with no limits, and no mention of
				 payment.
			-"Why would he sign such a thing?" I asked.
			 "They forced him to!"
			-"Who is this Ophilis Ses?" I asked, "A member of the gangs?"
				-Libak told us he is said to be the leader of the Tang Zen. He's rumored to be a
				 snakeman, and his organization is said to have taken control of the local snakemen
				 cartels.
			-I informed them I had a. . . family matter of my own to deal with, but (somewhat slyly)
			 suggested that Blade would of course wish to remain, the contract being tantamount to
			 slavery.

10/14/21: A Solo Adventure
	-On the way out of Nexus, you ordered your armor and bought demon summoning equipment, leaving
	 one cage setup stored at Rishi's.
	-For the trip, I again headed to Nexus's docks, and found a ship going West down the Yanaze.
		-My pockets a bit heavier right now, I booked a room on a luxurious yacht going that way.
		-Powered by magical contrivances, this boat was quite quick, and I disbarked only a day
		 later, to head South from the river.
		-The towns I passed seemed untroubled, not plagued by whatever is going on amongst the
		 Marukani further South. No reports of the undead or the like.
	-As I neared the manse, the surrounding are seemed strangely. . . silent.
		-No herdsmen with their sheep, even few natural sounds. . .
		-At the manse itself, I could not hear the usual sound of prayers.
		-The place was quiet, save the occasional shout, in unison, of training monks.
		-As I walked up to the entrance to the monastery, I saw one of my monks, Sister Lian,
		 standing guard at the door.
			-As I approached, she said, "Thank the gods you're here! He showed up, and he's let us
			 do nothing else since."
			 "Who is he?"
			 "Brother Jiaho found. . . some kind of entrance at the back of a closet. He removed
			  the stone, but only made it a short distance within before alarms sounded, and he
			  turned back.
			  From the back of the closet, though, later, a light shown. . . and _he_ came. He
			  looked just like statues of. . . you, before. He wears a horrible suit, like a
			  demon writhing around him.
			  He knows all the signs and mudras, but he is not like you."
			 "You said he let you do nothing else. . . Other than what?"
			 "He said we were too weak to be his followers, and makes us train. . ."
			 "Where is he having you train?"
			 "In the courtyard, but he waits below."
		-She took me to to the closet, where a stone removed from the floor revealed a stairway
		 going downward.
			-I went creeping down the stairs.
			-At the bottom of the stairs, there was only swirling light.
			-I had no idea what it might be, but he had emerged from it, and I boldly strode into
			 it.
			-On the other side (Of what? Am I still in the manse?), I found myself in a hallway.
				-It smelled. . . weird, dank and acrid.
			-It lead to a room on the right, and then a stair up at the end of the hallway.
			-Peeking around the corner of the room's door revealed a large chamber, and a. . .
			 humanoid of some kind.
				-It was covered in swirling, writhing gold, and was looking away from me.
				-It stood before a doorway, through which I could see some kind of tube, made of
				 some golden translucent material.
				-It noticed me, and spun it's head 180 degrees, then followed that with it's feet,
				 and began to walk towards me. The swirling gold covering his face then pulled back,
				 revealing the face of Larquen.
				 "So, you must be the reincarnation. You bear the hearthstone. Why are you so weak?"
				 "You are not Larquen Quen."
				 "I am, a backup copy. I retain most powers, but am missing one thing. It was supposed
				  to be mine. . .
				  It does not matter. What are you going to do with it?"
				 "I am going to do what I am fated to do: restore the glory of the lost First Age."
				 "Have you forgotten what was intended? Why rebuild a glorious age that never
				  existed? We can forge an empire instead!"
				 "To rule, but to what end? You speak of power for it's own sake. . ."
				 "What other sake is there? I have been reduced greatly, but I, I still remember how
				  to wield some powers. Not my greatest magics, but still much of the sorcery I've
				  learned. I must know, will you join me, with Creation's mandate, and forge an
				  Empire?"
				 "First, what last do you remember?"
				 "The final configuration of this project, before Quen retreated to a manse to the
				  North."
				 "I saw his last moments. You seek to repeat the same mistakes."
				 "We can bring a new age. We can rebuild, and we wouldn't be alone. Come."
				-I had strode towards him, over the course of our conversation. Now, he led me into
				 the room he'd been standing before.
					-It contained dozens and dozens of golden tanks, each containing a humanoid figure,
					 and a swirling golden mass.
					-Many of them are cracked or broken, containing only rot and bones.
				-Again, he spoke, demanding, "Join me. We will forge a glorious empire."
				 "Creation cries out for it, but how do you mean to do it?"
				 "The people of this age are weak. They will be easy to conquer."
				 "Why conquest, though? So many just need aid, guidance."
				 "It is necessary. It will show them their place."
				 "The world cries out for a savior, not another conquerer."
				 "It will show them we are above them. They _will_ know their savior."
				 ". . . I think you are intent on making the same mistakes. There is so much to
				  learn, but I do not think you want to."
				-He then tried what I recognized as Peacock Shadow Eyes on me, to no effect."
				-Recognizing it, I fell into Snake Style, to a look of astonishment on his face. It
				 seemed he could not believe I'd defy him.
					-He dodged several attacks, with a surprisingly malleable form, bending inhumanly,
					 then collapsing into a puddle to dodge by swipes, before forming into a great,
					 fanged maw and trying to bite me.
					-As I dodged the maw, a single claw swipe in passing finally connected, dealing
					 it a small wound.
					-Suprisingly, that led to him yielding.
				-"Wait, we need not fight!" he said. "I see that you are the stronger. We can still
				  work together."
				 "Is that so? To what end?"
				 "Whatever happened here damaged the dragon lines. I was only able to rouse and send
				  out three from here."
				 "Send them out for what?"
				 "To understand.
				  We do not need to fight. We can work together. I knew Quen's power, what you
				  are capable of. I recognize you are now strong enough to kill me."
				 "I would rather not have to. So much has already been lost."
				 "That's why you should listen."
				 "How do you mean to stand atop such an empire, personally? If the Exaltation should
				  have been yours. . . it is not. How now?"
				 "The Underworld holds great power. Power we can use."
				 "You would not stand atop that empire. You and I both know the price of the
				  Underworld's power."
				 "That deal was offered to Quen, not to you."
				 "Would it differ, for another?"
				 "It could. What would you give up for power?"
				 "A thing I know all too well, and a question near to my mind. But service to the
				  Neverborn. . . I would not accept. It would not be power I gained."
				 "Things have changed. Where is the nearest Shadowlands?"
				 "Thorns, at least, is one such. Why?"
				 "Where is Thorns?"
				 I described it's location, Southwest along the coast from here, to him.
				 "If you wish to learn Necromancy, go there."
				 "Not the easiest thing to do. I have heard fearsome things of it's ruler."
				 "What Solar rules there?"
				 "No Solar. A servant of the neverborn, perhaps a ghost."
				 "What is a ghost to us?"
				 "I have known exalts that walk in fear of it. I would not discount it out of hand."
				 "Where do Solars rule? What of the Solar deliberative? That trouble in the South
				  couldn't have impacted things elsewhere."
				 "It is cast down, and centuries gone. I know of no survivors."
				 "Really? Then none can stand in our way!"
				 "There are the Dragon-blooded, who purged the Solars."
				 "Dragon-blooded?!? Purging Solars? Hmm. . .
				  We should wake the others."
				 "First. . . what are you? What am I dealing with?"
				 "Put simply, I am a clone, a bio-$something replicant. Something failed. . . I
				  didn't capture the Exaltation. . .
				  I've retained access to my knowledge, though, my martial arts and basic spells."
				 "Could you make more such creations?
				 "I could make more, but no sample from Quen would still be good, unless Quen's body
				  could be found."
				 "You could make these from anyone?"
				 "Yes. I could make copies of you, or others. It. . . comforts me that you would
				  not be able to do so without me.
				  But, without. . . certain surgical procedures, they would be blanks. Still useful,
				  if you can train them, though.
				  With materials, I could also form more of these chao-morphic symbiotes."
				 "I had wondered what that was. It is not a thing I remember Larquen using."
				 "It is not a thing we were meant to use long."
				-He then walked over to another door, off the great room, opening it to reveal a
				 laboratory, filled with surgical equipment, and other devices.
					-Including some grisly, preserved organs.
					-And some equally grisly books, judging from the titles and diagrams on those I
					 glanced at.
					-"Lacking materials for further symbiotes," he went on, "Perhaps we should focus
					  first on new clones. Do you have a circle?"
					 "Yes, I do."
					 "Get the Dawn Caste's DNA. We will use it to make warriors. I regret to inform
					  you that none in this manse are worthy, though. All were once Tiger Warriors.
					  It is a shame to see them in this sorry state."
					 "As I said, I once thought life in this manse was hard. If this was as far as
					  the world had fallen, I would count us lucky."
					 "Show me then. Take me somewhere. Show me what we're dealing with."
	-He then led me back through the swirling light, and up the stairs leading back to the manse's
	 closet.
	-Lian still stood near the top of the stairs. He walked up to her, looked at her for a moment,
	 and then said, "I told you to bow when I approach. He then kicked her in the kneecap, shattering
	 it, and she collapsed.
		-I grabbed him by the shoulder, yelling, "That is not your place!"
		-His face twisted with rage, which he quickly masked, saying, "I cannot talk to you when you
		 are displaying unearned compassion like this. I will await you outside."
		-I went to Lian, and called two monks over to help her.
		-I told them there is much to learn here, but also much danger, and followed him out the door.
	-Outside, another Larquen-clone was walking up, with a woman, quite clearly a deathknight.
		-Much of her black wardrobe was seemingly corsetted with bones and studded with strange black
		 metal. Across her back she wore a wicked looking daiklaive.
			-Image of her: https://discord.com/channels/@me/772891797726822481/898398879735746600
		-The approaching clone addressed the one I'd me, saying, "Number 1, who is this?"
		 "I am The First Light's Dragon." I confidently asserted.
		 He looked at me with surpise, saying, "You're the one. Interesting."
		-The woman then looked to me, smiled, and said, "I've heard of you. . . A very strange tale
		 indeed. I heard you were responsible for attacking Lord Hilo's domain, in search of another
		 of my kind. Did you rescue her from the fey?"
		 "Not quite. . . Vestiges of the fey's bonds remain. . . Who, though, are you?"
		 "I have no name. What would you call me?"
		 "I name you deathknight."
		 "That's what you would call me?"
		 "I would call you what you are called."
		 "Then know me as The Maiden of the Mirthless Smile. I led the vanguard at Thorns."
		 "I see. I know someone who would very much like to meet you." I said, earning me the
		 aforementioned smile. "And I see one of the clones has brough you here." Looking to them,
		 I asked, "Why was that?"
		 The new arrival, who'd brought her, then said, "She seemed to know much of the area, and
		 to understand. Number One would wish to talk with her."
		 #1: "She did not attack you?"
		 #3: "She tried. I see you faced trouble of your own." To me, "You are mighty to have landed
			  such a blow."
		 "Well then," I said, turning to the deathknight, "What have you come to tell us?"
		 "I am more concern with what you would tell me, of where my sister is."
		 "Is she so dear to you?"
		 "No. I would slit her throat if you have not done it for me. But, if she lives, our master
		  wishes her return."
		 "Who do you serve?"
		 "The Mask of Winters."
		-Seeing a grimace on my face, in response to that, and then silence, she turned, and made as
		 if to leave.
		-"Hold!" I shouted, "This is a secret place."
		 "I will tell no one. On my honor."
		 "Even your master?"
		 "I will tell him nothing he does not already know. . ."
		 "What does that mean?"
		-At that, she only smirked, and took off running.
	-Garn gave chase.
		-Turning to look at me over her shoulder, I could now see a Dawn caste mark on her forehead,
		 though one seeping a black. . . vapor, rather than shining.
		-She then _vastly_ increased her speed, leaving a red blur behind her.
		-In response, I spoke, saying, "The dragon takes wing." And with that, my suspended casting
		 of Stormwind Rider was made manifest, and I was swept up into a racing whirlwind, still
		 giving chase.
		-That netted me only a horrible laugh, though, as she _still_ put on speed, and grew the gap.
		-Eventually, she raced _down a cliff_ and away, shaking my pursuit.
	-Shouting behind me, a clone caught up, now only a short distance behind me.
		-I whirled around and back towards him and, dismissing the spell, dropped to the earth, my
		 rage plain on my face.
		-"How could you expose this place so?!?"
		 "I defeated her. She is weak, and she brought only knowledge of Necromancy."
		 "And if she returns with an army?"
		 "There is one here."
		 "You had called them weak. . ."
		 "All the more reason to awaken the others."
		 ". . . She said something about what her master already knew. Do you know what she was
		  talking about?"
		 "Yes. I assisted her in summoning a ghost, through which we sent word to her master. I
		  could not summon her master, though. . .
		  I would not worry. She could not overcome you, and ran."
		-I returned with (apparently) clone #3 to the door of the monastery, where #1 waited for us.
		-As we approached, he began to question #3, asking, "What was this equipment she wore? The
		  strange metal?"
		 "She called it Soulsteel, taken from the Labyrinth."
		 "Meherrin was right, then, and it has it's own material. . . I wonder what it's properties
		  are."
		 "She was generous, and gave me this," #3 said, holding up a black torc. "She said her
		  master would not miss it. It has aunique property."
			-Putting it on his arm, he threw a punch at the air. As he did so, the torc let out a
			 horrible, cacophonous wail.
		-"Fascinating," the first clones stated, "Can I see it?"
		 "There is no need. You can see it from there."
		 "I am the first, your master."
		 "You are not my master. . ."
	-A fight ensued between them.
		-They both employed Snake Style, in combination with weird, shapeshifting strikes,
		 enabled by their symbiotes.
		-#1: "Respect me!"
		 #3: "I am the greater! My own master!"
		-I was quite content to look on. One of these clones is nearly as useful to me as two,
		 and far less dangerous.
		-In the course of it, clone #3 lost the torc, it flying to the side.
		-Eventually, one fell to his knees, with the other tearing him apart with his claws,
		 and then _eating_ him, with his symbiote maw.
		-He then grabbed the torc, mumbling, "Mine. . ."
		-I'm fairly sure #1 survived, but it's hard to tell.
			-That _may_ be the neck wound I dealt him, but many other gashes have joined it.
	-I was still enraged, shouting at the wounded survivor, "A powerful enemy, invited here!"
	 "All the more reason we should awaken the others. If you would listen to me. . . We
	  should gather the required materials."
	 "I. . . would know more of this proces. What is this material you speak of?"
	 "We need vitriol from Malfeas."
	 "Something a summoned demon could provide?"
	 "No, they cannot carry it with them. You must enter Malfeas. I am now mortal, and would
	  not survive, but your Exaltation would preserve you."
	 "I would need a way. How does one enter Malfeas?"
	 "I know a ritual." he said, striding off. "It is already prepared."
	 "I would know more of this ritual. One should not jump headlong into hell. If I could bring my
	  circle. . ."
	-He led me inside the monastery's grounds as we spoke, and then into one of the buildings.
		-There, in a room within, the clone gestured to a disembowled, but still living, monk, his
		 entrails strewn in about the room in what looked like careful lines and patterns.
		-It was Brother Huan, a friend. Close in age, we'd trained together for many years.
		-The clone simply walked past him, to a table, and began sorting through papers and grisly
		 instruments, babbling about how it would be a five day walk, to Malfeas and back, for me,
		 but that time passes differently there, and that the ritual would ensure my return mere
		 minutes after my departure.
		-In my rage, I barely heard him, and I strode towards his turned back.
		-Despite my stomping, he was so proud of his ritual and preoccupied with it that he remained
		 oblivious pushing the claws into his throat and tearing, continuing until I had ripped his
		 head off.
		-In response, the symbiote shrieked, fell away, and then slithered over the disembowled
		 form of Brother Huan.
			-He began screaming as the thing covered him, his intestines slithering back in.
			-Eventually, his form entirely covered in the golden mass, he stood.
			-Stepping toward me, the symbiote retreated from his face, as he grabbed me and hugged
			 me, saying, "It. . . I don't know how. . . it has healed me?"
	-I led him out the door of the building, calling over two of the more junior monks to help him.
		-As I did, the gold slowly melted _into_ him, until it was no longer in evidence.
		-The two monks I'd called over led him off, to get some rest, at very least.
		-As they stepped away, I gestured to another monk, a senior thaumaturge, calling him over
		 to me.
			-"Keep watch over Brother Huan," I said. "He has been exposed to something unknown, of
			 The First Age, that golden thing our. . . late visitor wielded. Let me know if there is
			 any change or development in his condition. I will be checking in regularly, even once
			 I leave here again."
	-I then gathered the rest of the monks in the courtyard to me.
		-"I'm here now. That. . . thing is gone.
		  It claimed, though, to have awaken three more of it's kind. Were there really only four
		  of them?"
			-A couple of monks spoke up, and, yes, as best any could tell, no more than that were
			 seen.
		-"What were those?" one among the crowd shouted to me.
		 "They are remnants of The First Age, another backup project in case The Last Light's Dragon
		  were to be destroyed. The project would seem to have failed, though. . .
		  They brought an outsider here, though. We are all in grave danger. She was a minion of The
		  Mask of Winters."
		-In response, another of the senior thaumaturges offered to surround the manse in wards
		 against the undead.
			-"Yes, make it so."
		-Addressing again the whole of the crowd, said, "Two more things! Tell me, by the fastest
		 means available if you see more of the clones. I will be checking in more regularly, via
		 the tree. And, don't go in that closet, or the passages beyond."
		-"You seem troubled," one of the monks called out. "Are we really in that much danger?"
		 "Yes. Very much so."
		 "We'll protect the manse. . . but we'll flee if we must, taking all the knowledge we can.
		  We can go to Nexus. It's where you'll be?"
		 "Yes. If you must flee, find me. As you know, you should be able to reach me, either at
		  the compound of Hawke's Chargers, or at Silver-Tongued Rishi's estate."
		-Another monk then called out, one who was trusted to travel outside the manse. He said,
		 "We have remained hidden so long, but I have met others, who could be of help."
			-He spoke of a cult of "illuminated ones", some of whome are in Nexus, and who seemed
			 to have a. . . compatible doctrine.
			-I've heard some word of such a cult, popular with the street people of Nexus, and
			 strong in the Firewander district.
			-Their beliefs, he told me, involved 5 promises, including that The First Age would fall,
			 but that the gods would still send champions, their shining ones. "Are you not one such?"
			 he asked me.
			-"There is wisdom in that suggestion," I told him.
			-He then instructed me as to how to find them, saying, "When last in Nexus, I met a man
			 named Joseph One-Shoe. He had nothing, but helped me when I dropped my things, returning
			 my things and coins to me. He stood with me while I gathered my things, and then took
			 me to get some tea. I found him in The Little Market of The Nexus District. Perhaps he
			 is the one you should seek."
			 "I shall. Allies are needed. I have met some I trust, but more will be needed with the
			  magnitude of the task before us.
			  We should also step up our recruitment, and the time may soon come when we will need to proselytize further."
	-The monk who suggested it then began work on wards against the undead, surrounding the manse.
		-It took him more than a day, pinning up paper strips with Old Realm sutras and
		 sprinkling powders in ritual patterns around the entire perimeter of the manse.
		-He was exhausted by the end of it, saying only, "It is done," and then collapsing where he
		 stood.
			-I asked a couple of the monks to carry him to his bed.
	-I stayed at the monastery for a couple more days, for my comfort and theirs.
		-There was one scare when a common hungry ghost passed through the wards, triggering alarms,
		 but it was successfully destroyed by the inner ward, happily confirming their efficacy.

10/25/21:
	-As I made my way back to Nexus, the others reunited at Hawke's compound, a week after we'd
	 returned to Nexus.
		-Silent Onyx had been looking into the silver monster, which turned out to be some strange
		 blob of liquid silver, emerging from the Wyld zone and doing various things. Following
		 people, absorbing them, sneaking around, etc.
		-I also heard what happened with Golden Blade, as it happened.
			-He killed a sewer monster that had been abducting children, likely the source of the body
			 parts in the water. Some mustached figure fled from the scene, though, so perhaps there
			 still exist conspirators.
			-In the course of that, he also acquired a follower, Sparrow, a young boy with a shaved head.
			-He was also jumped, in revenge for our assault on Lord Hilo, though dealt with them easily.
		-Pip had also found an ally, at some place called "The Tomb of the Night", but was unwilling
		 to say more where others might hear.
			-It _does_ sound like she may have again revealed her Solar nature, to an even bigger
			 crowd.
			-The others went with her to this place, finding it beneath a bridge she led them to.
			-They were greeted there by a strange, green-ish woman, speaking in pidgen.
			-Pip indicated to her these were friends she had brought, to the delight of the woman.
			-She insisted on touching each of them. As she did so, a caste mark on her forhead flared,
			 a simple golden circle, like Silent Onyx's.
			-It was she that noticed the child, Blade's follower, who remarked at her caste mark,
			 with wide eyes, saying, "She's _another_ illuminated?!?"
			-Blade tried to dismiss the child, sending him back to Hawke's compound, but the strange
			 woman insisted he stay, saying the area is dangerous.
			-She led them into a dark passage. Soon, an _impossibly_ dark passage. Something was
			 strange there.
			-Eventually, she led them to a small, dimly lit room, with several doors opening onto
			 it. In fact, _strangely_ lit, seemingly black and white, leeched of all color. Perhaps
			 the result of warped essence flows?
			-Is this one of the six Solar tombs of Nexus? "The Tomb of Night" is one such, and it's
			 said to swallow whole those who step into it's darkness.
				-Pip confirmed it was indeed the tomb.
				-It appears to be a manse as well. Perhaps this Night Caste woman is attuned to it.
			-In any event, the strange woman indicated the place was safe, and introduced herslef as
			 Hyula.
			-Pip then began to speak of Ophilis Ses, saying he'd gained control over all of Nexus's
			 gangs, and had killed Hyula's lover. This is the source of their alliance, as
			 Hyula desires revenge.
			-Pip also said she met one Silver Wind, an anathema hunter. Uh oh.
			-Thankfully, Pip had learned many things of the snakemen gang, learning the location of
			 many snakeman hideouts in the Firewander district, and that some of them were keeping
			 profits for Ses, a potential wedge to use.
			-Unfortunately, she and her mother are also now homeless, their home having been burned
			 by the snakemen.
			-Golden Blade then reached out to me, checking on my ETA.
				-Reaching the river by Agatae, I had found a fishing boat to ride back into Nexus
				 on, and was only a few hours away. I arranged to meet them soon.
			-The room was also filled with paper covered in crude writing, but detailed maps,
			 apparently Hyula's investigations into Ses.
				-They ran through the locations of Tang Zen hideouts that Pip and Hyula knew.
				-One of which was curiously right on top of the sewer where Blade fought his monster.
			-They discussed how best to get to Ophilis Ses, and Hyula volunteered that he had a
			 boyfriend, somewhere outside Nexus, and a son, who is currently missing.
			-I arrived around that time, and Blade, Libak, and Hyula went out to fetch me.
			-As she led all of us back into the tomb, I asked her how she and Pip had met. She
			 pointed to her caste mark and then to me. "Yes," I responded, our kind does indeed seem
			 to be drawn together.
			-All of us reunited, Hyula then spoke of what went on at several of the Tan Zen sites.
				-Their armory held many weapons, bearing a finely wrought pattern, some kind of set.
				-At their "factories", one near the sewer with Blade's monster, they _make_ monsters.
					-Golden Blade described a thing made from stitched together corpses.
			-I also asked Pip for some details of this anathema hunter, and what people saw of her.
				-She indicated 200 plus people may have seen something they shouldn't have.
				-She did not know if this hunter was of the Wyld Hunt, but did not think so.
	-In our pursuit of Ophilis Ses, we decided to raid the site the Tang Zen were keeping slaves,
	 an issue of personal concern to Libak and Blade both.
		-As we traveled, the city was clearly troubled. The homeless, in particular, bore improvised
		 arms, guarding barricades built of trash.
		-The Tang Zen site was in The Brood Market, a slave market in the city.
		-Stepping into this place of suffering, though, Libak flew into a rage.
		-He strode towards one of the slavers, taking bids, and punched him straight in the face,
		 scattering the coins on his table.
		-Golden Blade also looked queasy at the sight of the market and, when Libak flew into his
		 rage, Blade held back for a moment, then shrugged, and joined in.
		-He ran to the slaves at the auction block, and began striking off their chains.
		-Libak continued his rampage while Golden Blade employed charms to both rally the freed
		 slaves into a unit and to disperse a group of mercenaries that was pushing towards us
		 through the crowd.
		-Well, this was neither what I signed up for nor what I expected binding myself closer to
		 the circle would mean, but they still _are_ my best allies in the face of the deathlord
		 that now threatens my home. I fell into Snake Style, and activated my Essence Fangs and
		 Scales Technique.
		-Pip, though, tried to tackle Libak, seemingly hoping to stop the rage.
		-While they brawled, I saw Silent Onyx slipping off. Running up to him, I asked him where
		 he was going.
		 "To complete our mission," he said.
		 "I'm with you, then."
	-Onyx and I found ourselves at the warehouse in question, marked with the their sign, three red
	 triangles.
		-I asked Onyx how he wanted to do with this and he simply said, "Silently."
		-I nodded, and said, "I'll be on those crates," pointing to some across the alley down the
		 street, "Just give me the sign." I continued on down the alley, sat on one of the crates,
		 and pulled a book out of my bag. I could see the warehouse's front door and a side door
		 from there.
		-Onyx inspected the building. It lacked windows, and the roof was strangely prepared, covered
		 in herbs and charcoal. Nearing the building, that seemed to be covering a smell, as it stank
		 of rotting meat.
		-Onyx relayed as much to me, and then crept in through the front door.
		-He returned a few minutes later, to report what he'd seen, and avoid someone moving about.
		-Inside were several zombies, packing boxes.
			-They were placing pouches of some liquid into the boxes, and then covering that with
			 other goods, concealing it.
			-Onyx retrieved one of them, giving it to me. I tucked it behind the crates I was sitting
			 on.
		-In another room, he also heard someone talking.
			-A man's voice, he mentioned a scalpel, sewing, and later something about finding the
			 children again, they being "the only thing I can work with." A muffled response, from a
			 woman, followed by movement, is what sent him out the door.
		-He returned inside, and looked further, attempting to sneak into the room the voices were
		 coming from.
			-He was overcome by the stench, though, and stumbled, attracting their attention.
			-Before he fled out the door, he saw a mustached man, bent over a small corpse with it's
			 lungs removed and splayed out around it. He was accompanied by another man, one with
			 a satchel of herbs and charcoal over his mouth and nose.
		-This relayed to me, we discussed our next move, settling on the other door.
			-With charms, Onyx slipped past the man working there, and listened at the metal slatted
			 rollup door there.
		-Uh oh. While this is going on, I got some sense that Golden Blade had revealed himself in
		 some manner, his anima flaring.
			-Shit. An immaculate monk soon showed up. Though one who lacks the House mark you'd
			 expect. . .
			-We rushed to them. It would take us two rounds to reach them.
			-Orrr. . . not? Silent Onyx and I arrived at the market, but could only remember what I
			 had felt through the Torc if I really concentrated. Here at the market, it was as if
			 it had never happened. And yet I was still there, for some reason?
				-I could feel similar confusion, through the Torc, from Golden Blade.
				-I vaguely recall Golden Blade dealing the monk a grevious blow. Perhaps this was
				 some power or ploy to escape? If so, it's. . . reach is, at least, somehow limited.
	-In any event, Blade and Libak continued beating the guard officer, that they had / had not
	 been interrupted in doing by that strange monk.
		-Once he dropped, Blade led the freed slaves to the Grand Canal.
		-Golden Blade shouted to them that they were now free, free to do as they will.
		-Libak added that, if they sought jobs, the Suli family could help. Golden Blade spoke up
		 again, shouting that work could be found for warriors at Hawke's compound.
		-Here I spoke up, saying that I don't think it would be wise to lead a crowd back to Hawke's
		 compound. "What happened here is likely to be a big problem for us, and I don't think
		 they'll want that falling on their heads too."
		-They heeded my advice, dispersing the slaves into groups and, and instructing those
		 interested in work with our suggestions to trickle in over time.
	-We then made our own way back to Hawke's compound, only to find the streets nearby deserted,
	 and our way blocked by a figure in a silver mask and white robes, The Emissary.
		-"You are wanted in my city by the armies of Heaven. For this I have cast out others. But I
		  can use you. I have need of you. Come with me."
		-It walked over to the nearest door, and opened it. Inside was not the shop interior one
		 would expect from the exterior, but rather an ornate, marble-clad room, far larger than the
		 building we had walked into.
		-We followed, and, inside, the emmissary removed it's mask, revealing the face of Itraxian,
		 The Weaver.
		-She seemed to know who we were, or were in The First Age, anyways.
		-She asked us for aid in ridding Nexus of the deathknights infesting it.
		-In particular, she asked if we knew of Ophilis Ses, claiming he is somehow the reincarnation
		 of Surin of Justice, another Eclipse Caste from The Invisible Manse.
		-Turning to me, she also said that, "He is working with the ghost of Larquen Quen, that
		 thing that calls itself The Mask of Winters."
		-"I swore long ago that I would not act, except to protect my city and it's ideals. My hand
		  has been forced.
		  I have never been one to employ violence to achieve my ends. I find myself unprepared for the organized force I now face."
		-She looked desperate, and tired.
		-"We can come to an accord," I said, "I am also troubled by The Mask, by the simple fact of
		  his existance, and in more concrete ways.
		-"First," she said, "You must swear an oath, not to reveal who I am."
		-"But how is it that you come to be here?" I asked. "When the others were trapped at The
		  Invisible Manse."
		 "Trapped? We weren't trapped. We were arrogant, too arrogant to admit we feared to leave.
		  After Larquen did that to Meherrin, I could not stay."
		-I was the first to assent to her oath, and each of the others swore it in turn.
		-I asked her then if she had a plan, to eliminate the deathknights in the city.
			-She told us of a Guild factor named Kan Dans, and where to find him.
			-He is a leader among a group known as The Cult of the Illuminated, who believe us to be
			 saviors sent by the gods.
			-The cult is a front. They help Solar Exalts, and eventually smuggle them out of the
			 city, most North, some South. Kan Dans and others in the cult, though, are actually
			 disguised Sidereals.
		-Silent Onyx then spoke up, volunteering that he knew where two Abyssals were, relaying
		 what we saw at the warehouse.
			-"Strange," Itraxian said, after a moment's concentration, "I can barely see this
			  building. . ."
		-Itraxian offered that she could protect us from the Wyld Hunt. She will issue a proclamation
		 forbidding them and their agents from the city.
			-"It may damage the markets, and the damage could be irreparable if the matter isn't
			  resolved within a couple of days. I don't see any other way, though. . ."

11/8/21: We meet The Cult of the Illuminated
	-Libak and Pip went to delicately explain our natures to Rishi & Hawke.
		-(They had to miss tonight's session, and are best skilled at social delicacy.)
		-What we're saying:
			-We're Solars.
			-We found a bit more than we admitted at the manse, pieces of our past. . .
			-We're going to be hunting Deathknights on behalf of The Emissary, but the deathknights
			 are also hunting for the one we captured.
	-Meanwhile, we asked further questions of The Emissary / Itraxian.
		-"As we look into the deathknigths, how do we reach you?" Golden Blade asked.
		 "If you call for me under the light of the sun, I will seek you."
		-What are these Sidereals you mentioned?
			-"They are the Chosen of Fate, and the architects of our betrayal.
			  Some among them, though, now work to aid Solars. They do not seek the Deliberative
			  restored, but to shape governance themselves.
			  They do not remember, remember how dangerous we can be. Only the eldest among them
			  could, and I only know of one such."
			 "Oh? And who is that?"
			 "I cannot say."
			 "You are sworn not to?"
			 "No. To say their name is to call the eyes of Heaven.
			  Every time your anima flares, the Sidereals have an opportunity to find you. In Heaven,
			  there is a great loom, woven by spiders. When your anima flares, they can spot you in
			  this web.
			  The cult _does_ help, though. Most solars are taken out of the city, but some are taken
			  beneath. To deep places my eyes cannot see. I've seen nearly a dozen young Solars taken
			  down there, but none have returned to the surface.
			  I have heard that members of this cult have defeated deathknights, in the North, and
			  have attacked The Realm's holdings in The Threshold. They were accompanied by shining
			  warriors in golden armor."
			-"Anything else you would warn us of?" Golden Blade asked her.
			 Her eyes glowed gold, briefly, and then she said, "I see people moving, from the armory
			 in The Little Market. They are moving boxes large enough to store a body in. . . "
			-"Before we go," I said, "you should know of another danger. Are you aware that one of
			  the fae dwells within the Firewander's Wyld Zone."
			 "I am."
			 "It speaks of it's minions eventually sweeping forth, rampaging across the surrouding area."
			 "No, I don't think it will be that dangerous soon, with the chimera chasing them."
			 "The chimera?"
			 "It's strange, it feels like Mithra, but looks nothing like them, and I sensed none of
			  the thoughts I'd associate with them. I have encountered Lunars known to me before,
			  and recognized them, but this, it felt. . . detached. Wild.
			  It has been hunting the fae and it's minions, though it does worry me when it leaves
			  the zone. It sometimes goes to the Nighthammer pool at night, absorbing people. Randomly,
			  from what I can tell."
			 "I have sworn myself it's enemy. I mean to see it dealt with."
			 "Ah, you're the one feeding it?"
			 "_Feeding_ it?"
			 "Yes. Each time it faces your opposition, it grows stronger."
			 "Stronger how?" Golden Blade asked.
			 "As you think of it, those thoughts creep into your dreams. In your dreams, a substance
			  called Gossamer forms, and it is harvesting it."
			 "How do we fight such a thing, then?" Golden Blade asked.
			 "With cold iron weapons. You slay it, as we did the Raksha of old."
			 "Good," I responded, "My plan remains unchanged, then."
	-We then opted to hustle over to the armory we'd heard of. It sounds like something is currently
	 under way there.
	-We took a trolley line, and, while on it, listened to word on the street.
		-No mention of the fight in the slave market.
		-Instead, everyone seemed to be talking about the explosions in The Firewander District.
			-There was mention of a glowing girl, battling a silver-clad ninja in a warehous and
			 spilling out onto the street.
			-Well, more or less the same problem. . . 
	-We passed through The Little Market on the way, and Golden Blade suggested looking into cold
	 iron weapons.
		-Golden Blade located a wholesaler of iron ore who was willing to sell small portions, from
		 which we could at least have cold iron weapons _made_.
		-Asking that merchant, he learned that smiths could be found in the market around us that
		 could handle that forging.
		-After Blade arranged the purchase, Onyx got our attention.
			-"Don't turn around. We're being watched."
			 "The Sidereals?" Blade asked.
			 "No. They're not very subtle."
			-We tried to duck out of sight, weaving between the merchant stalls and darting down
			 alleyways.
			-In the course of it, Blade and I lost sight of Onyx, but we could see we'd not shaken
			 our pursuers.
			-They wore silver turbans, and silver sashes, both around their waste and across their
			 faces.
			-There was a crash behind us, and then, suddenly, Blade's friend Sparrow was at his side.
			 "Sparrow!" Blade shouted, "I thought I told you to stay safe!"
			 "I am safe! My friend is here, but says it _is_ very dangeous out on the street today."
				-Onyx later told us he'd seen someone come to our aid, stabbing upwards at what
				 appeared to be the leader of our pursuers as they ran across the clothes roofing
				 the market, presumably this "friend".
	-We followed Sparrow, who led us to a nearby street that had collapsed into the sewers below.
		-Going to a ladder placed there, he led us into the sewers, which strangely grew _cleaner_
		 as we went deeper.
		-As we went, we saw copies of a flyer scattered about, and, grabbing a largely intact
		 copy, I read through it.
			-See "Hand Written Flyer" in Roll20.
			-Those promises are awfully promising (heh).
		-Eventually, we came to an underground tram station, being used as a kind of homeless
		 camp.
			-Sparrow led us to a kid sitting between kegs of a black powder, firedust. He was
			 pouring it by the handful into smaller jars.
			-"You don't have any fire, do you?" he asked, to which we shook our heads.
			-Sparrow introduced us to the child as "more illuminated ones", which got a wide-eyed
			 response from the kid.
			-"Have you heard the promises of Shen Aru?" the new kid asked. "They speak of the
			  shining ones, come to save us, but who will be weak from the long journey from
			  Heaven, and in need of our help.
			  That's why I'm making bombs.
			  Don't worry. You're safe down here now."
			 "Maybe not," Blade said, "Given what hunts us."
			 "I know what hunts you. I've been hunted too. . ."
		-An adult then approached, and introduced himself as Joseph One-Shoe."
			-"I have watched you for some time," he said. Turning to me, "You were the
			  hardest, always traveling back and forth to that manse of yours. There are
			  better ways to do so, you know."
			 "I'm all ears," I responded, "Though I know of some better ways, better is
			  often. . . flashier, and it's not wise to attract too much attention."
			 "That is exactly why I did not reach out, fearing to draw the attention of 
			  watchful eyes. Looks like that attention came to us anyways," he said, looking
			  hard at Sparrow.
			-"Where is the one called Pip?" he then asked.
			 "With a friend of ours," Golden Blade responded.
			-"That. . . thing that has hunted you has proved more effective at the task

			  her."
			 "What is that thing?" Blade asked.
			 "I do not know. For a long time, I thought it was one of the Sidereals, but it
			  does not seem to be. It is. . . outside Fate. A mystery. You do seem to
			  accumulate those."
			-"You should train with us," he continued. "You could learn, learn to hide from
			  the eyes of Heaven."
			 "Though you seem to have heard much of us," I said, "We've heard but little of you.
			  Tell us more, about yourselves and your organization."
			 "Walk with me," he responded.
		-We walked some 15 minutes, through various corridors, until we came to a great
		 flowing river of raw sewage.
			-"You must first demonstrate your humility," he said, and then leaped into the
			 river of shit.
			-Wading out towards the center of it, he dove, and then did not surface.
			-Silent Onyx was pretty firm about it now being time to go home, but Golden
			 Blade claimed he'd smelled worse on the battlefield.
			 "After you, then," I said.
			-Blade indeed climbed in. I removed my buff jacket, leaving it folded in the

			-I will refrain from describing this in the detail that Lesley did.
			-Out towards the center of the flow, we could indeed feel an opening, with a
			 slight suction.
			-Diving down, it led to a lower chamber, draining through a grate there.
