			 by some kind of beast.
			-Joseph too stood there, and he was casting a spell, which I recognized as Open
			 the Spirit Door.
		-The passage open, we went inside, finding a place far different from the sewers
		 surrounding it. Inside was a building, surrounded by greenery, though with
		 pipes meeting above, forming a ceiling.
			-At the doorway to the building stood a lion, far larger than a natural one and
			 apparently made of gold.

			 not be allowed to enter until night fall."
			-I shrugged, and sat, cross-legged, on the ground beside him.
			-With plenty of time (and thus mote regeneration) on hand, I took a moment to
			 look around with Spirit-Detecting Glance, this being a spirit's sanctum and all.
				-We were indeed surround by dematerialized spirits, _stray cat_ spirits,
				 and, in fact, now that you looked close, several actual stray cats, lounging
				 in the area.

			 "What?!?" I asked, "What happened?"
			 "Rishi was having a party. Talking with him, it seemed he already knew what we were.

			 "Our invitation came with enemies on our heels," I replied. "The shit was the same,

		-We had no further time for discussion, though, as the door opened, and the lion moved aside.

			-I hurried forward to join them in it.

				  They are my family, and they have accepted you. I will protect you."

				 was an impressive and moving performance.
				-It got pretty intense, and some of the. . . heartier adults of the crowd began to
				 scourge themselves with lengths of beaded and braided hair, as Nylia said, "Cleanse

				-As she spoke, the crowd repeated it, amplifying her voice.

				 sorcerous initiations and many shamanic rituals.
			-I quite enthusiastically joined in, at a table inside the bar.
				-Though I was drinking without getting drunk. I eventually did get a bit of a stomach
				 ache, as the bug began to stir more.
				-Actually, no one in the crowd seemed very drunk, but they do seem to be feeling
				 _something_.
				-I spent quite a bit of time talking with them about their theology.
					-Most of their beliefs are derived from The Promises.
					-They also a concept of "personal illumination".
						-Pressed on it, they described taking _immense_ quantities of Bright
						 Morning, as Shen Aru had done (not strictly necessary, but the most common
						 option, as it's traditional), while self-flagellating and otherwise self-
						 depriving. They then write down what they see, sharing it with others of
						 the cult, and try to repeat various methods reputed to yield good results.
			-Much of the cult seemed to have been rather down-and-out before they Exalted.
			-Through out all of this, they have been painfully frank and honest about themselves,
			 and other hard subjects.
				-I knew many of my circle could identify lies with Charms, and from their quite
				 evident skepticism, I imagine they tried, but no one ever reported anything.
			-A common thread in their beliefs is that the current system isn't working, and that
			 The Illuminated are here to cast it down and rebuild it.
			-They don't seem to be in full agreement about what to rebuild, ranging from anarchists,
			 to technocrats, some believing in the supremacy of the Illuminated, or others in that
			 they are here to serve and protect humanity.
			-They do, though, all seem united in the belief that it was through _humanity_, not the
			 Terrestrial Exalted, that Creation has endured through this Age of Sorrows.
			-To Golden Blade's especial delight, they're definitely against slavery.

11/22/21:
	-I had my discussion with Joseph One-Shoe, from the TODO above, while we drank after the
	 ceremony.
	-We also found a moment to corner Libak and Pip, and learned a bit more about The Mistress of
	 Pacts Sealed in Blood's new freedom.
		-Libak, apparently, was unable to bear watching her suffer, enslaved, any longer, and
		 released her himself.
		-Thankfully, he wasn't _completely_ idiotic about it.
			-He extracted promises of no retaliation, sanctified by Pip's Eclipse caste ability.
			-She, meanwhile, claims to be intent on escaping The Mask of Winters, and wishes to

				-Well, that's eminently compatible with what you, and the rest of the circle, seek.
				-If we can indeed trust her, we still may have an ally here.

				 probably going to be one tainted with rationalization and justifications.
	-Nissen, Black Powder Jack, and Jasara the Wise are the ones among the cult who champion most
	 strongly the three broad strains of New Age the various members seek.
		-Nissen envisions an age of anarchy, where all are equal.
		-Jasara is essentially an anarcho-capitalist, though she believes it will somehow be filled
		 with individual operators, and has various ideas how to prevent guilds from dominating.
		-Black Powder Jack is more or less an anarcho-communist, with some vague, hand-wavy notions
		 as to how they'll maintain important freedoms.
		-All, though, believe that the Solars are not meant to _lead_, but to enact the will of
		 humanity.
	-Another circle of Solars among the cult seemed very interested
		-Aslag, who we met earlier, seeks to eliminate resource scarcity in Creation, and has ideas
		 as to how.
		-Kismet, an Eclipse Caste artificer, is interested in AI, and who seeks to rebuild the
		 (instant) messaging system of The Old realm.
		-Kouf Thengi, of the Dawn Caste, seeks a new defensive grid, or access to the Realm's.
	-In talking with that circle, I mentioned that I did indeed remember some of the created
	 intelligences of The First Age.
		-The whole crowd reacted to that with silence, shocked looks on their faces.
			-Those we'd just been introduced to as one's who remembered portions of their past lives
			 feigned shock too! Hmm. . .
		-Joseph then stepped in, saying, "Our friend must be confused. I'm sure you all remember the
		 first time you had Bright Morning. . ."
		-Rylea, too, spoke to the crowd, and seemed to be doing something with essence as she did,
		 calming the onlookers as she said, "Yes, you all know how the Bright Morning affects you."
		-Golden Blade, despite me quickly kicking him as he spoke up, insisted she was lying, that
		 these _were_ memories.

		 remember. Remember a better world, better with you in it. One where the Solars brought about
		 wonders."

			 restoration is my fondest dream."

				 terrible things, committed atrocities."
				-Golden Blade: "I remember instead terrible things done _to_ me. We're not judged
								for the sins of past lives. There's no sense in it!"
				-Me: "We are given great power. But that does not mean we cannot fail. . ."
				-Joseph then spoke up, saying, "I would not have gathered you all here if I thought
				  you were monsters."
					-Of course, but Golden Blade frowned at this, and asked what he meant.
					 Joseph: "I do not think you are the monster the Immaculate Faith claims you
					          are."
					 Golden Blade: "Obviously not. But, some we call monsters, they simply hunt.
									Could we not easily be counted among such forces of nature?"
					 Joseph: "I have met demons, it's true. But I have not met one of your kind who
							  behaved like one."

						 Stargazer: "Gods?!? You're barely Exalted! I don't know why we're wasting our time on such trash."
						 Blade: "Barely Exalted?!? Care to test that?"

						  Perhaps another test. A hunt. . .

12/6/21:
	-While we were waiting to get started, I learned a bit more from Lesley about the laboratory in
	 the monastery's basement.
		-There are 500 clone tanks, 150 of which remain occupied.
		-_Each_ tank had a symbiote, so you retain 497.
	-We began the session back at Hawke's compound.
		-Scouts were still steadily reporting back in.
		-All of our target areas appear to have been hit, by Hawke's men or the cultists.
		-Most of the fighting ended up limited to the Nexus district, with some happening
		 around the Nighthammer district's arsenal as well.
		-We also heard more signs of The Great Contagion, not seen since the dawning of The Age of
		 Sorrows.
			-Also some weirdness that _may_ just be that, around the Nexus coliseum.
				-Reports talked of monsters as well as illness, though the former may simply be
				 fever dreams.
	-We adjourned for a bit back to Golden Blade's room, to use the Wound-Mending Needles to heal
	 (most of) my wounds.
	-Golden Blade suggested isolating Hawke, to prevent the spread of sickness.
		-As he stepped out into hall, though, there was already a runner lying, feverish, on the
		 floor of the hallways.
		-We dragged those we found, Hawke included, to a room, isolating them a bit.
	-We resolved to see to matters at the coliseum, as monsters may be a direly urgent matter, and
	 then to see what we could do about the disease outbreak.
		-Our Panacea Pipe has great promise, but we need to learn more to use it.
		-Pip (not here for the session) volunteered to stay behind and tend to the ill among the
		 mercenaries.
	-As we stepped out of the compound, there was some faint. . . noise, in the air.
		-Listening closely, it sounded like discordant piping, and whisper. Whispers like we've
		 heard since our exposure to the black mirror. . .
		-It came from the direction of the coliseum. I guess our course was clear.
	-We comandeered an empty canal boat, though Golden Blade promptly smashed it into another.
	-Comandeering a unsmashed third, we lifted it's unconscious and shivering owner from it, Blade
	 tucking some money into the man's pocket.
	-This time, Blade had more success poling it along.
	-Soon, as we passed beneath a bridge, we saw a still running trolly going overhead. Knowing it
	 ran towards the coliseum, we all lept up to the bridge above, and climbed aboard it.
		-It was still full of passengers, all unconscious and feverish. This works quick. . .
		-As the automated cable car made it's stops, we unloaded them, reasoning we did not need to
		 bring them closer to harm.
		-Indeed, as we got closer to the arena, not only did the sound grow louder, but people on the
		 street seemed to be sicker, many now lying clearly dead.
	-As we got off the trolly at it it's terminous, the cacaphony had grown loud, and even rats
	 seemed to have fallen sick the moment they crawled up onto the street.
		-This close, I could also no longer feel the prayers of my cult, drowned out in the noise.
	-The arena's gates were clogged with bodies, what seemed to be the remnants of a crowd trying
	 to escape.
		-It would prove necessary to climb the coliseum's walls to enter.
		-Blade and I powered up, while Onyx scouted ahead, scaling the walls.
		-He was soon back, reporting what he saw.
			-Inside the arena, there was a pack of zombie-looking dogs, and some horrible,
			 stitched-corpse giant, standing 20' high.
			-The sound seemed to come from beneath the fighting pit's flooring, clamorously loud.
		-Silent Onyx wisely recommended avoiding that mess, if possible.
		-We searcehd the outside of the arena, and Blade spotted a grate covering a large sewer
		 pipe running into the arena.
			-Presumably used when flooding the arena for the naval battles they occasionally host.
		-Golden Blade quickly ripped the grate from the stonework, and we entered the sewer.
	-The sewer indeed led into the coliseum. A short way in, we took a stair up, and found ourselves
	 in a corpse-choked hallway.
		-The corpses soon began to stir, though, rising as undead, and battle was joined.
		-Onyx cut down a few and then, adjusting my claws, I stepped into the fray and became a
		 blender. Mere seconds later, I stood panting, covered in blood and surounded by severed
		 body parts.
		-Blade then stepped over the corpses and, walking into the room they'd emerged from, his
		 glowing caste mark illuminated the source of the noise.
		-There before him stood an abomination, nearly a dozen children stitched together, their
		 lungs pulled from their backs and stitched into a slowly pulsating nightmare-organ, the
		 source of the noise.
		-From behind it too, a red light began to glow, revealing another deathknight, the mustached
		 "physician" Onyx and I had encountered before, and undoubtedly the creator of these
		 abominations.
		-The bastard that made this thing being too far for me to reach immediately, I ran at his
		 abominable creation, attempting to rend it apart. It proved surprisingly tough and dense,
		 though, with only one swipe from my claws doing any apparent damage, tearing some of it's
		 stiches.
		-Onyx joined me in that experiencing similarly limited success, though the thing was
		 starting to show it's wear.
		-The horror on hand apparently not being enough, the deathknight opened his mouth and
		 shoved a meathook down his throat, then pulled it back out, drawing forth a swarm of ghosts
		 with it.
		-Blade joined us in wailing on the noise machine, finally silencing, though perhaps not
		 destroying, it.
		-That sorted for the moment, at least, I lept over it and the ghosts, using a pillar to
		 redirect myself at the deathknight, plunging my claws into his chest.
			-As my right hand struck home, the wound quickly dissolved into liquid gore, forcing
			 the claw back out and reforming, healed.
			-The second, though, plunged in deep, and, though a similar thing began to occur, he
			 seemed unable to reform, instead collapsing into a pool of gore.
			-As that happened, the ghosts turned back to him, falling on the corpse link hungry
			 dogs, dragging his body off with them into the darkness.
		-Onyx and Blade then finished off the cacaphony abomination.
	-With the thing quieted, we could now here the sounds of people on the street above, sounding
	 like some life returning to the city.
	-The area down here had been turned into some kind of necromantic amplification chamber, and I
	 was interested in studying the works of our enemies. As such, we sent Onyx above, to see both
	 what happened to the undead titan above and to see if the destruction of _this_ abomination had
	 solved the illness.
	-Onyx came back a short while later, reporting that, indeed, the city's health seemed to be
	 restored, and, though it did not fall with it's creator, The Emissary had arrived and dealt
	 with the titan above (seeming a bit pissed, he said, that we'd left it to her).
	-We then sent him back out again, back to Hawke's compound, to retrieve squad of Hawke's men to
	 secure this area.
		-While waiting on their return, I had some time to go through what was here.
		-There were many texts covering surgery, and other, more gruesome topics, diagrams for
		 strange, necromantic weapons. I gathered up what I could.
		-It appeared hastily set up, rather than something that had been here long.
	-It was Nissen who found us first, though. He was happy to report the deaths of a further three
	 deathknights, all the cult knew of in the city.
		-He also asked that, seeing as The Illuminated had fulfilled their end of the bargain, were
		 we ready to go train with them?
		-I cautioned him that we wished to check in with our allies and. . . one other, but said that
		 then, yes, we'd be willing to join them for the training.
		-He nodded and said that he'd work on burning the bodies above, then, so that ghosts do not
		 rise, while we waited for Hawke's men.
		-I bundled up the necromancer's writings that I found in a scrap of cloth, and then went to
		 help him in that. As they arrived and saw us, Hawke's men wordlessly joined in.
	-During that, Blade pulled me aside for a bit. We found a secluded spot and called out to The
	 Emissary, beneath the light of the sun. We reported that all deathknights we'd learned of were
	 now dead, and asking if she knew of any more.
		-By way of response, images of The Emissary appeared all around the city, on street corners
		 and rooftops. She/it announced that a new law was being made for Nexus: The Wyld Hunt and
		 The Immaculate Order are henceforth banned from the city of Nexus, and Solars are welcome
		 and to be given sanctuary. (!!!)
	-That done, we assented to the cultist's training, and we were given a week to settle our affairs.
		-At their suggestion, we let Hawke know we were going to be with the cult, so he could contact
		 us in an emergency.
		-To me, they mentioned they'd send a circle to watch over my monastery, and to inform the
		 monks where I was. I told them I'd speak with them myself, but, upon using my wooden face,
		 I could see that Aslag, Kismet, and Kouf, Solar's we'd met among the cultists, were already
		 there.
	-With matters settled, we traveled beneath the city, and began our training.
		-On the first day, they shaved our heads (those that had not already, anyways) and eyebrows.
		 They also announced that our diets would be restricted to rice and tubers.
		-Kicked awake the next morning, we were dragged out for prayer. We were instructed to hold
		 martial arts stances throughout the prayers, hit with sticks when we faltered.
			-Just like childhood thus far!
			-During this, we were provided nothing but water with an oily sheen on it, and we quickly
			 began to hullucinate.
			-The prayers were over _us_, praying to heaven to guide us on our paths.
			-We were to remain until every mortal left.
		-The remainder of that day, and the latter half of many days that followed, consisted of a
		 tour of the sewers, each location requiring us to do something disgusting, much like wading
		 in shit to get to the sanctuary in the first place.
		-We trained for _three years_.
		-We saw parts of the sewers we'd never would have suspected existed. Archery ranges, combat
		 dojos, and obstacle courses.
		-A major focus of the training was on how to destabilize areas, rally followers, and spread
		 their brand of revolution.
		-For the first year, we were woken up before anyone else, and sent to scavenge for scraps of
		 garbage, to feed us and the rest of the cult.
		-As our training progressed, each of us had many mortal cultists tell us a personal secret
		 and pledge loyalty to us. That bond was then tested, and we were trained in the skills we'd
		 need to manage these groups of followers.
			-We're all going to be gaining some dots in the Followers background.
		-For the second year, we were each made to pick a "calling" with in the cult to train further
		 with. They are:
				Oyabun: The leaders of the underground Sanctuary who live on the streets among creations lowest, witnessing firsthand the struggles of creations denizens and working to help the people who need it most. They are trained to be social engineers, capable of helping creation to a better tomorrow, where everybody is equal.

				Kyodai: The street Messiahs of the sanctuary who feed the homeless and run a series of soup kitchens to feed and assist the most vulnerable of creation. They give vocational training to people and help them to organize. Their training focuses on self sustainability and the creation of  localized renewable systems from farms to power grids. 

				Shatei: The Warriors of the sanctuary, effectively protest organizers and organized resistance recruiters, they have the ability to take an unorganized mob and turn them into guerrillas capable of bringing down governments from within. These revolutionaries speak of a better tomorrow, and how creation will be better for it, but to make that tomorrow a reality they must be willing to fight for their ideals and stand against the tyrants who would take advantage of the people!
		-I chose Oyabun.

		-For the third year, they had us track dangerous foes, monsters, Immaculate monks, and the

1/3/22:
	-During our training downtime, an older Sideral named Kai (who seems to be a bit insane) _knew_
	 we had the mirror, and approached us about it.
		-He'd been studying the Abyssals and The Deathlords.
		-He intends to form a strike force, to act against The Mask of Winters, and strike a blow
		 against the Deathlords.
		-He believes The Black Mirror will be integral to that task, and understanding Abyssals,
		 saying it was "fated to be so."
		-He arranged to have Waters the Fields with Blood look into it and he became, to all we
		 could see, a Solar.
		-It did not last, though, and, when he returned to his dark self, shadowland-energey and
		 ravenous spectres flooded forth from him, thankfully contained by wards, but limiting
		 further study of this.
		-Kai knew the mirror had been been dug from where the primordial Perfect Principal of
		 Consumption had been slain.
	-The Cult has warned us that, as we've grown more powerful, we've grown easier to spot for those
	 watching Fate.
		-In particular, any flare of our anima or charm with the Obvious keyword gives them a chance.
		-A d10 is then rolled, and if it's less than your essence, it's spotted.
	-It is also no secret to us that we've quickly become the most powerful circle in The Cult's
	 training camp.
	-While we've trained, Nexus has thrived, despite some issues.
		-Our battle with the Deathknights in the city shook things up a bit, and The Emissary's
		 proclamation provoked a backlash from merchants convinced they'd been doomed to destruction
		 by The Wyld Hunt.
		-Hawke's Chargers have risen in prominence, but word got out about his contract, with rivals
	     impeding the works projects Hawke was initiating, hoping to claim ground.
		-Trade, though, has thrived on the turmoil.
		-The Cult of the Illuminated has been pushing into places vacated by the banished Immaculate
		 Order, spreading rumors they were to blame for the Deathknight incursion.
		-There seems to have been a scandal affecting Libak's family, a cousin linked to organized
		 crime, the snakeman Ophilis Ses.
			-Through a mix of The Cult and spies in Golden Blade's employ, we've learned things
			 about him that few know.
			-His Tang Zen are apparently actually based out of Great Forks, and he is the lover of
			 a Solar from that city, Azure Path.
			-The Tang Zen are small in number, but highly influential throughout The Riverlands.
	-The power The Cult is most concerned about is The Mask of Winters.
		-There have been many skirmishes between his forces and The Marukani.
		-One of his Deathknights sits on The Council of the Concordant, and has been waging the
		 same war diplomatically, claiming the the towns The Mask has seized have joined the rule
		 of Thorns willingly.
		-Many of The Riverlands' powers are sympathetic to that, fearing that, should Lookshy get
		 involved, it would heavily disrupt the province.
	-At one point, Ayesha, who initiated you into The Celestial Circle, asked if you planned to
	 return to manse in the North.
		-I responded, "Yes. There is much left to uncover there."
		-In response, she summoned a silvery gateway, and led me within, past the Celestial Lions
		 and into Yu-Shan.
		-Within the heavenly city, she led me to a jade dome, with lines of spirits waiting to get
		 in, and took me inside, to a doorway.
			-She addressed the Celestial Lions guarding the dooway, saying we were on business for
			 "The Forbidden Manse of Ivy".
		-That led out onto the frozen, windswept valley before The Invisible Manse, opening a door
		 in the side of a mountain there, to the skyship hanger we'd seen on it's blueprints.
		-Inside was a grisly scene, the long desicatted corpses of dead dragonborn, one bearing what
		 I recognized Meherrin's spear, and a craft shaped like a seed.
		-With the hearthstone, I was able to activate the ship.
			-It proved to be a Manta-Class Transport (Wonders of the Lost Age pg. 43).
		-Ayesha, piloting it, took it out of it's berth, and into the sky.
		-The next part, I was asked not to repeat. Ayesha took the craft down into a lake, our
		 surroundings dissolved into flowers, and, when the receded, we were a mile from Nexus,
		 on the river.
			-Quite the trick.
		-Before bringing it into the city, though, she had another question for me, saying that,
		 "Your companion Libak's fate is clouded, difficult to see. You have a choice, though. If
		  this spear is returned to him, his path may grow. . . dark, drenched in blood. Would you
		  return this to him? Or deliver it to me, and spare him that?"
		 "Well, I know what he would chose, if that is so, and I will assent to his choice. Here."
		 "You must not tell him of this, then."
		 "I will not bring it up. If he asks, though. . . he may well see through me. See that he
		  does not ask."
			-Hmm. . . 
		-Back in Nexus, she provided us with the service of a suitable crew for the skyship.
	-After we completed our training, we got word from three brothers, Illuminated monks.
		-A member of their cell had been captured, held by the local horselord and an Immaculate
		 official, and they mean to burn her at the stake.
		-With the skyship, we can reach there in time, and we quickly debated a plan.
			-We opted to disguise ourselves as traveling traders, to enter the town without alerting
			 them (obviously setting the skyship down somewhere out of sight).
	-After four hours travel and concealing the grounded ship, we approached what, to all appearances,
	 seemed to be a normal village.
		-Well, walking around, _one_ building stood out, it being substantially fortified.
			-Outside stood an Immaculate Monk, praying, and from within drifted the scent of
			 inscence.
		-Pip strode boldy up to one of the guards at the door, introducing herself as a trader,
		 newly arrived.
		-The guard called within, to his lord, asking him if he had need of traders. I did not hear
		 the muffled response, but we were then admitted.
		-That was followed by a search of our possessions by the guards within.
			-We were wise enough to bring packs of various innocuous goods, though they still
			 confiscated many higher value items, like bars of soap. When questioned, the one word
			 response was "taxes".
			-We then had a brief audience with the horse lord within, Himvul, but he had no interest
			 in our uninteresting goods and we were soon dismissed.
				-When Pip asked what the lord _would_ wish, he responded that he desired the herbs
				 necessary to test if someone was a witch.
		-While we were busy with that, Silent Onyx and Sparrow looked through the village.
			-It's primary resource was soon apparent, as the trees that surrounded the villlage were
			 in fact _ironwood_ trees, and many things in the village were made from it.
			-It was also obvious where the "witch" was likely kept, for there was a bell tower with
			 no bell, and instead barred windows and a guard.
			-The also found markings associated with The Cult of the Illuminated on one building.
			-The villagers, though, seemed to be half-starved, and the vegetable gardens around the
			 town seemed stricken with some kind of blight.
		-As we caught up about that, we spotted some commotion in the market place, a guard
		 harassing a peasant and merchant, demanding more "taxes".
			-By the time Libak intervened, the guard was threatening to cut off the peasant's finger
			 in lieu of the tax he did not have.
			-Libak paid a bribe to the guard, claiming business with them that he wished to urgently
			 attend to.
			-Both were grateful, and we later spoke with the merchant within his home.
			-He spoke of Himvul's depredations, that bandits Himvul was paying off with the majority
			 of their ironwood, and the futility of the situation.
			-He did mention an "idealist" Dao who sought to change this all, but did not hold much
			 hope. He was willing to direct us to Dao, but said he could do little to help, being
			 preoccupied with his brother's hard times, his brother's wife, Kerala, having been taken
			 by Lord Himvul. Accussed of witchcraft, he claimed she'd sacrificed a child to some 
			 cult of the dead, and the lord awaited a magistrate, to try and sentence her.
		-We went off in search of Dao, only to see a pair emerging from the house we were directed to.
			-One supported the other, who appeared to be drunk, and was certainly in tears.
			-Libak asked him what was wrong, while a third villager, quite similar in appearance to
			 the pair and, as he approached, made to Sparrow a Cult of the Illuminated recognition
			 sign, one which was quickly returned.
			-This latecomer then ushered us all over to his home. He stated he'd recognized young
			 Sparrow as a "brother", and Pip chimed in that we were "kin" as well.
			-We learned the story of Kerala. She had been wont to take the village children on walks
			 in the wilderness, identifying useful herbs. One afternoon, the boy with her was bitten
			 by a snake. She tried to suck the venom from the wound, and, failing that, opened it
			 wider, to let the venom flow out with the blood. The child died, and she was found, with
			 blood on her face and singing an ancient song, one the village once used to send off
			 their dead. They called it a sacrifice.
			-"Used to?" Libak asked, "What happened?"
			-The Immaculate Order ended that when it came. It slew their priest, and cut the tongues
			 from all who knew the old songs, save Kerala who none but the priest knew had learned
			 them. When Lord Himvul exalted, they sent a priest here to stay, to guide him.
	-Pip decided to start up a couple of word-of-mouth campaigns, against both the abuse of taxes
	 and The Immaculate Faith.
		-Meanwhile, I spent my time investigating the blight affecting the town's foodstuffs.
			-The food crops, _and only the food crops_ were affected by a fungus. Examining it with
			 Essence Sense, though, made apparent that the fungus propogated along patterns
			 suggestive of the land's finest ley lines. I suspected the work of necrotic wood essence,
			 emanating from one of Creation's dragon lines. But while such a thing could be an 
			 intentional attack, the formation of shadowlands or corruption of key manses would
			 necessarily cause such harm, whatever goal or random chance may have caused that.
		-Blade, meanwhile, detailed some of his toops, sending them out as scouts into the surrounding
		 area in search of the bandits.
			-Well, he tried to, anyways, but, upon returning to the ship, he found they had a captive,
			 bearing the emblem of a red eye on a white mountain.
				-He was indeed a bandit, and the emblem was that of his company.
				-Blade interrogated him (with Judge's Ear).
					-They seem to have spiritual backing: "By the glory of Mother Bog. . ."
					-He mentioned selling the occupants of some previous town to the fey, at which
					 point Golden Blade became pissed, and the captive was disarmed (and then beaten
					 to death with said arm).
					-Turning to his men, "Give me another one."
		-Silent Onyx cased the old bell tower.
	-Gathering again, we discussed what we'd each done, and our next steps.
		-It seems we've made good progress formenting rebellion against the horse lord, but no real
		 progress filling any resulting vacuum.
		-I advocated looking into the horse god of the Marukani. One of his hairs is the traditional
		 marker of Marukani nobility. Perhaps he can be found and bargained with.
			-Asking Dao, he knew tales of the god, despite Immaculate supression, integral as it
			 was to Marukani culture.
			-The hairs were rewards for acts of heroism undertaken in the sacred mountains. A horse,
			 something this especially poor Marukani town lacks outside the horse lord's private
			 stock, would also go a very long ways to help one's cause, given the god and culture.
			-I had proposed Dao for the role, but the circle pointed out that Kerala also fit, and
			 had, with the dying boy, already committed an arguable act of heroism.
		-We also discussed substituting Pip or myself with Kerala, via Flawlessly Impenetrable
		 Disguise, freeing her to seek her elevation.

1/31/22:
	-We continued to debate our course of action in this town, and settled on a general goal of
	 elevating Kerala in Himvul's place, as horse lord of the village.
		-To that end, Pip employed her subtle social manipulations to burnish the image of both Kerala
		 and the traditional Marukani ways.

		 the aid of Yflea.

		 also the sort of thing Kerala's knowledge of local spirit lore might aid.
		-As such, we decided we'd free her. Several of us could manage a suitable disguise, to replace
		 her in prison, but none could sneak in and out quite like Silent Onyx, so he volunteered to
		 take her place.
			-(James was also not responding until half way through the session, so it seemed a good
			 way to tuck Silent Onyx away.)
			-A short while later, I indeed got to meet her for the first time, as she met us at the
			 appointed spot outside of town.
			-She carries herself like a noble, at least, even garbed as a peasant. Good material to
			 work with, for our coup here.
	-So, we headed back to our ship, intending to fetch Yflea from Nexus.
		-Arriving there, though, Blade's troops informed us that there'd been futher attacks.
			-Not by bandits, though, but by strange humanoid figures made from swamp debris, aided
			 by animated vines.
			-Such things sounded like elementals or demons to me, though I did not know the specific
			 type. They seemed, though, to likely be related to the bandit's in the area, since the
			 captive one had mentioned a "Mother Bog".
		-Leaving Blade and his troops behind to backup Silent Onyx as needed, we boarded the ship
		 and flew to Nexus.
			-Looking down as we flew, we saw much activity in the land. Bands of Lookshy troops and
			 horsemen with Marukani banners were seen on the move, heading Southwest.
				-No doubt towards Thorns. . .
				-Most such bands were all of one nation, but we did see some mixed groups, and
				 interesting indicator of the politcal winds.
			-Arriving in Nexus, I went to the training camp, to retrieve Yflea and help him load his
			 equipment aboard the ship, what he'll need for the geomantic rituals.
			-Meanwhile, Libak had indicated he wanted to check in on his family, and he went to take
			 care of that. I _had_ heard they were having some trouble (see notes above). . .
			-Pip too wanted to check on her mother, so we decided to all meet back at the ship in
			 two hours.
	-Pip returned to the ship in a rage, saying her mother had been taken be triad members, who may
	 have delivered her to the Tang Zen. She meant to find them, rescue her mother, and _hurt_ them.
		-I agreed with her the matter was urgent, and so we sent Yflea and the ship's crew off back
		 to the village.
			-Yflea was to begin his investigation under the protection of Golden Blade's men, and
			 the crew was to return here with Blade.
		-Meanwhile, through our allies, we sought word of Tang Zen hideouts in the Firewander
		 district, learning of five of them.
			-Pip was definitely in a rage, threatening great displays of Solar wrath. Libak, Blade,
			 and I tried to convince her discretion might be wise, but I'm not sure that we were
			 successful.
		-We then sought out the first of their hideouts, with Pip running straight up to the door
		 and banging on it, threatening death to all inside, if her questions are not answered (and,
		 also, once they are).
			-A small bar, people soon began to stream out of it, running and screaming.
			-Others, though, stood up from their stools and drew knives, with the bartender yelling,
			 "You can _try_ to kill us, anathema! We won't yield!"
			-The inside of the bar was soon painted with blood, but Libak had spared one, who he
			 dragged to a back room to interrogate.
				-I meanwhile wiped blood off myself while Pip and Blade rummaged through the bottles
				 at the bar and drank.
			-Libak came out, still clearly shaken, asking us not to kill the man who booked it out
			 the front door without looking at us.
				-I asked Libak what he'd learned, and he said the man had claimed _not_ to work for
				 the Tang Zen, though we're still convinced the triad he's a member of is. He _also_
				 claimed that, when in town, Ophilis Ses stays at a jail in the district.
				-Ses is quite the target. Perhaps we can cut the head off this snake, or at least
				 gain all the leverage we could desire to secure the release of Pip's mother.
		-We then went in search of the jail.
			-As we did so, The Penitent found us, saying that her spies had heard of the action at
			 the bar (James showed up after being AWOL, so he's playing her while Silent Onyx is in
			 that tower).
			-Mercenaries known as The Hooded Executioners, sometimes called "The Black Cloaks",
			 perform policing duties in the Firewander, and are likely the ones _supposed_ to be
			 running this jail.
			-Pip was eager, but the rest of us thought it best to look into what sort of arrangement
			 they might have with the Tang Zen.
				-Eh, did a fair amount of debating, but ultimately didn't learn much before we headed
				 to the prison.
			-Heading to the jail, we once again opted for the "front door" approach.
			-This time, though, Pip was willing to talk first, thought she took a direct approach,
			 asking directly for Ophilis Ses.
			-That yielded, from the guard, a "Leave." He then began trying push Pip back out the door.
			-There was some commotion, then, and a new voice from inside the door: "Let them in. I've
			 been expecting them."
				-A thing Libak noted was true.
				-In the foyer stood a richly dressed snakeman with copper scales, who indeed proved
				 to be Ophilis Ses.
				-He claimed that the men sent to fetch Pip's mother were incompetent, and are now
				 dead, their heads on pikes in the yard. He claimed she has not been harmed.
					-Turning to Libak, he nodded at that.
				-Pip asked to see her, to which he assented, sending the door guard to retrieve her.
				-When she came, she seemed to have been treated well.
				-He also claimed that bringing her was the only way to protect her, but that received
				 a grimace from Libak.
				-He said something about having gotten what he wanted, asking us if we knew what would
				 come after us. Pip responded yes, and he replied that we were either very brave or
				 very stupid. . .
				-He then said, "Well, I expect you wish to take me into custody?"
				 "Yes," Pip replied.
				 "I will go with you, then, if you'll promise not to harm me."
				 "You did not harm my mother, so I will assent."
				 "Very well. The oath is sanctified," he said, as his anima flared.
				-He then explained that he had simply wished to speak to us.
					-He knew of our shared past, and of the manse.
					-He asked us to join with him, to kill Itraxian, blaming her for never returning
					 to us, after seeing our dragonblooded persecutors brought low by The Great
					 Contagion. "She could have told us! We could have restored Creation to it's
					 lost glory!"
					-Our circle was united in opposition.
						-"Why divide ourselves against one another, given the forces arrayed against
						 us?" I asked. "You blame her for not giving you the chance to restore
						 Creation. Why not seize the chance you have now?"
						 "She took from me what's mine!"
						 "What's yours?"
						 "Hollow! Don't you remember?!? I _built_ this city! I laid it's first
						 foundations with my bare hands!"
					-We also argued with him that he was identifying _way_ too much with his past
					 incarnation.
						-"I think neither you nor I would wish for me to claim every perogative
						 Larquen Quen did. . ."
					-We tried arguing too that Itraxian had protected the city from The Wyld Hunt,
					 but he responded that he'd done far more than she ever did.
						-"What did you do?" Pip asked.
						 "Set in motion plans that took time to come to fruition. I just needed you
						 here."
					-We suddenly felt it neccessary to check on The Emissary, stepping out and
					 looking up, to see Itraxian in the sky having a crazy martial arts battle in
					 the air with four other figures.
					-"Who are those figures?" I asked, "The Hunt? Yours?"
					 "They didn't know who she was, and thus could not marshal the proper forces. I
					 told them who she was."
					 "The Sidereals, then."
					 "The masters of The Wyld Hunt."
					-We fell to arguing among ourselves, about whether to aid Itraxian, what to do
					 about Ses, etc.
						-As we did so, we witnessed flash of rainbow light above as one of the
						 figures struck Itraxian, shattering the mask of The Emissary from her face.
						 Her caste mark then flared, as she was surrounded by an anima banner of
						 golden light.
							-This was soon followed by shouts on the street: "The Emissary! She's
							 an anathema!"
					-Eventually, we decided there was likely little we could do about anyone
					 threatening a millenia-old Solar, even if we could reach them in the sky, and
					 that we still wished to hold onto Ophilis Ses.
						-We thought it best to take him to The Cult of the Illuminated, but Blade
						 asked him if that is what he expected, and Ophilis responded, "Yes."
						-We tried binding him with the Manacles of Night, but, as he predicted,
						 they would not close around his wrists: "It is no longer in my nature to
						 be a prisoner, and Creation agrees."
						-Hmm. . .
					-We at least began to lead him out of the prison.
						-The streets were in chaos, as rioting and panic broke out.
						-He, meanwhile, brought his brandy bottle.
	-As we walked out, one of the figures battling Itraxian was cast down from the sky, shattering
	 several buildings he flew through.
		-Nonetheless, the figured stood, bloody but alive. He was garbed as an Immaculate Monk, but
		 his eyes glowed purple, and he had a matching halo.
		-This was our opportunity, if we're to help Itraxian. Looking at each other, it seemed we
		 were all resolved to do so, as we fell into stances and the like.


2/14/22: A St. Valentine's Day Massacre
	-I myself fell into Snake Form, as the Wyld Hunter slowly got to his feat.
	-The monk-garbed assassin, seeing three of my companions suddenly glow as their anima flared,
	 turned to us, and lept forward, bizzarely throwing a paper crane at Pip as he did so.
		-The crane left a minor cut wound across her shoulder, but the world also seemed to. . .
		 twist as it did so. The world around us grew gray and murky, and the crane soared back off
		 into that murk.
	-Pip and The Penitent swung at the monk, who now glowed, with a red circle on his forehead, but
	 there blows seemed to pass through his form.
	-Blade met no greater success with his own strike, despite cleverly kicking up a paving stone
	 as a distraction prior to it.
		-However, the red glow grew brighter, and a strange band of white silk appeared from the
		 murk, wrapping around Blade and pulling him closer to the monk.
	-With my wooden claws twisting, forming a great single blade on each hand, I wove in between
	 Pip and Ses, twisting to suddenly strike at the monk.
		-My attacks were countered seemingly differently, with ribbons of white silk emerging from
		 the murk to pull each of my hands away at the last moment.
		-This felt familiar. . . a martial arts technique that I. . . no, that Larquen had once
		 dueled against.
		-"I can keep this up all day!" I shouted, adding, "Can you?"
	-The Emissary above now resembled a many-armed golden goddess, and was continuing her battle with
	 the others.
	-It seems the Immaculate Sidereal knew all manner of ways to dodge an attack, demonstrating at
	 least three as we all tried again and again to land a blow.
	-Libak tried a different tack, and had greater success _offending_ the monk, as he shouted
	 insults leading to a seeming change in the murk, swirling suddenly more intensely around Libak.
	-Golden Blade then managed to burst the silk bands he was wrapped in, but still could not land
	 a blow.
	-This all continued on for some time.
		-Attacks fueled by essence, though, seemed to evoke a different counter, the silk-from-the-
		 mist diverting them. Each seemed to get a bit closer.
	-Wearing or bored, the Immaculate monk suddenly disappeared, reappearing in a flurry of cherry
	 blossoms and paper cranes, near a fountain some 20 meters away.
		-This felt a bit familiar, the blossoms reminding me of how Ayesha got the airship back to
		 Nexus so quickly. More confirmation they're both Sidereals? Or indicative of some other
		 connection.
	-Despite us at least distracting this one, Itraxian's battle with the remaining two monks in the
	 sky did not seem to be going well.
		-She kicked one of them hard enough that it seems she killed him, but, while doing so, the
		 other got behind her, stabbing her near her kidney.
		-Seemingly in response, the crowd of scared onlookers around us all clutched the same part
		 of their chests, and we could hear cries of anguish all over the city. . .
			-Clearly there's some kind of sympathetic magic at play here. The Emissary is very much
			 thought of as the patron of Nexus. . .
	-Blade then lept at the grounded monk, closing the distance in an instance, and attempting to
	 tackle him. However, he collided with the fountain's statue instead, toppling it from it's
	 plinth.
	-The monk responded by reaching out towards Blade with his palm, the murk briefly disappearing
	 as he did so. Blade managed to interpose his blade (heh), and the hand left a melted print on
	 his daiklaive.
	-I reached him next, running up onto the fountain and leaping at him, clawed hands forward.
		-Finally, the right one connected, drawing first blood.
		-The claws of that hand sunk into part of his chest, but he seemed staggered more than I
		 would have expected from the wound.
		-It also now dawned on me what his motions and dodges reminded me: the way the Wyld
		 itself fights, chaotic forms driven by a story. Here his personal fortitude finally failed
		 him, his story giving way before the story of the dragon.
	-Seeing the connection between the city and it's Emissary, Libak sought to rally the people
	 nearby, leading them in a prayer to The Unconquered Sun, in support of Itraxian.
		-It was quite the performance, and The Emissary indeed seemed to rally, landing a tremendous
		 blow on one of her remaining attackers, punching his spine right out of his back.
		-The other, though, glowed purple, and split into many doubles of himself.
	-It would seem our monk didn't care for the sight of his own blood, as he turned to me, saying,
	 "For that, you will suffer like none have ever suffered before."
		-A dubious assertion, given that he's no lord of Malfeas or the like, but he clearly had a
		 plan to at least try and make good on that, as he reached out towards my forehead with two
		 glowing fingers.
		-I thankfully leaned back just in time, and then quickly forward with a flurry of clawed
		 strikes, though all were deflected by his suddenly-there silks.
	-Before he could try anything else, Pip also landed a blow, cutting his body in twain.
	-His body, though, dissolved into rose petals, leaving only his clothes, a few paper cranes, and
	 a nine foot long sutra.
		-Written in blood and tears on fine white silk, it is the tail of a maiden born with three
		 faces, who saw all of her life at once.
		-I recognized it as a martial arts parable, one that could allow someone attuned to this
		 artifact to activate multiple forms at once.
			-A thing Pip can make good use of.
	-The foe at hand resolved, we again looked up, just in time to see Itraxian dealt a grevious
	 blow from her remaining opponent's sword , though she tore him in half in response.
		-The sword remained, though, piercing her breast, and she sagged, then fell from the sky.
		-Pip, Libak, and I all rushed to where she fell nearby, with me pulling open my robes as
		 I ran.
		-As I got to where she lay unconscious amidst rubble on the street, my passenger emerged
		 from my chest, scuttling over to her and burrowing into her flesh.
		-While the bottlebug worked, eventually pushing the sword out and poking the occasional
		 insect legs out to pull her wounds closed, I reached out to my Wooden Face under The Cult's
		 control, telling the cultist monitoring it that, "One of the Shining Ones is in dire
		 trouble, wounded and beset by enemies! Send soldiers and doctors!"
			-I then directed them to where we are in Nexus.
	-Within ten minutes, Nissen, Jack, and Nassara, all ranking Solars in The Cult, were there with
	 us, and helping to tend to Itraxian's wounds. 20 minutes after that, she was again conscious
	 and on her feet.
	-Libak then brought Ses over to Itraxian, introducing him as "the one that sold you out."
	-"Surin," she greeted him, "I wish it was a pleasure to see you. I thought I had banned you
	 from the city."
	 "Sure," he responded, "If you can keep me out."
	 "I swore I would never raise a hand against my circlemates. . ."
	 He grinned at that, and added, "They all refuses to aid me in killing you, you know."
	 "So," he said, "Another offer: I have my own circle, and, while you were busy with this,
	 they took control of the dams around the city. Acknowledge me as the greatest among you,
	 swearing yourselves to me, or I will drown the city."
	-We fell to shouting for a bit, at Ses and among ourselves.
	-Eventually, we all seemed quite intent on ending Ses's misanthropic life (fuck his deal),
	 though I wondered if we needed him to save the city.
	-Pip, though, said that _she_, at least, could take no part, though she encouraged us. She said
	 that she would meanwhile try to do something about the dam, and started asking questions about
	 how she could get there quickest.
		-Ah, there was something I could help with, and perhaps save the city. I told her I would go
		 with her, and spoke the trigger phrase to call up a whirlwind for us.
		-The next problem, though, was that the city of Nexus didn't have any dams. . .
		-As we were born aloft through the city, though, golden images of Itraxian guided us,
		 pointing the way.
		-She led us to the Nighthammer district, to a white First Age building at the very Western
		 edge of the peninsula on which the city rests.
		-Atop the building, there was some newer construction, ramshackle shanties. The door of one
		 of them had been torn off, and there were streaks of blood all around it, but no bodies.
		-Rushing inside, Pip and I descended into the original building, then following a hallway
		 for something like a quarter mile, until we could hear rushing water above us.
		-The streaks of blood led this way, as if bodies were dragged down the corridor.
		-Eventually, along with the smell of gore, we could smell spiced smoke, and we emerged into
		 a viscera-filled room.
			-There was a great altar, constructed from the bones of the mutilated corpses around the
			 room, and draped in their organs. Atop it lay another snake man, dead from a knife in
			 his chest.
		-Along one wall, an illuminated screen showed a warning in Old Realm, speaking of activation
		 of the dam and imminent overflow.
			-The axe buried in the machine it was attached to probably wasn't helping things.
		-I tried to understand the machinery before me, to see if there was something I could do.
			-This was a matter of the utmost importance, and I gave it my all. 
			-As I did so, a more metaphorical dam broke, and it was as if I'd operated such things
			 many times. I began to operate the controls as if by rote.
				-Pip later told me that, during this, I carried myself. . . differently, proud and
				 sinuously fluid in my movements. Not unlike someone else I know all too
				 intimately. . .
			-I was able to slow the dam's closing, activate some kind of warning, and activate the
			 city's sentinel defense force, to aid in the evacuation. I was not, however, able to
			 stop the process.
			-More screens then came to life, showing various parts of the city. Sewer covers were
			 flying off, and metal soldiers emerging from the sewers and ushering people down the
			 streets.
				-They seemed to employ a strange, invisible force, herding people with it.
			-We could also hear the warning that was broadcast, in Old Realm, talking of the closing
			 dam.
				-Pip asked if I could change it to Rivertongue and I nodded, engaging the manual
				 override and recording mode.
				-In Rivertongue, she warned the city's populace of the coming clood, telling them
				 to take their things and flee the city to high ground.
	-Pip and I then took our own advice, and fled the city in another whirlwind, stopping to help
	 her mother escape as we went.
	-Outside the city, we could see a great wall of light form, cutting off the Nighthammer district
	 from the rest of the city, and blocking the flow of water. Within hours, the water had risen
	 some sixty feet above the low lying city, the Nighthammer long since innundated.
	-Eventually, the wall of light flickered, and gave out, and a great wave smashed through Nexus.
		-The heights of some of the city's hills remained undamaged, and some other First Age
		 buildings survived as well, but the vast majority of the city was flattened.
		-Even among those who did not escape in time, though, there were many survivors, protected
		 by the invisible force of the metal sentinels.
		-This devestation must have also extended far up and down the Yellow, Grey, and Yanaze rivers,
		 one of (perhaps _the_) most densely populated areas of Creation. . .
	-While Pip and I observed the city, we also saw flashes to the West.
		-They came from the Imperial Mountain, which soon began to display a red glow.
		-In fact, the same glow appeared at various points around the city, forming into a woman,
		 clad in scarlet.
		-Then, she spoke: "In my absence, you have grown complacent. As such, you will be punished.
		 You will serve the Scarlet Empress forever. I am the Scarlet Empress reborn."
		-With that, all of the images disappeared, save the great one over the Imperial Mountain.
		-Five minutes later, a column of elemental energy shot up from the Imperial Mountain, arcing
		 down to some place in the South. It shone brightly for an hour, and then dimmed.
	-Outside the city, Pip and I debated what we should do next (we not having yet reunited with
	 the others.
		-I favored contacting Itraxian and The Cult of the Illuminated both, to see what we could do
		 to help the city.
		-As we spoke of her beneath the sun, though, Itraxian came to us.
		-"Rebuilding Nexus," she said, "Will not be possible. The Realm is going to invade. Their
		 ships are already on the way."
			-I suppose they can't exactly ignore what happened here.
		-"What, then," I asked, "Are the thousands, millions here to do?"
		 "I know of a place," she replied, "Where they can go. Denandsor, the City of Makers."
		 "I remember. . . met you there. . ."
			-Clearly, Larquen had been there (see references to Denandsor above).


2/28/22:
	-Nexus is a sodden ruin.
		-Left homeless are around 640,000 refugees.
		-We (jokingly?) discussed torturing the ghost of Ses.
		-No one has seen or heard from Rishi, though Hawke has been trying to locate him.
	-Over the first day, the Emissary rested.
	-Over the second, though, she appeared as a golden light to nearly everyone in the city, guiding
	 them to useful supplies. Food, medicine, and even, aiding me personally, the precious stone and
	 gems from the Blessed Isle required for an amalgam. . .
	-The Solars of The Cult of the Illuminated also provided a great deal of aid too.
		-Black Powder Jack even showed a flare for construction, raising earthworks and wooden
		 structures from diagrams comprised of freshcut saplings.
		-We also began mass summonings of demons together, beginning with bottle bugs to aid the
		 wounded.
	-The night of that second day, we reached out to Onyx, via our shared dreams.
		-We broke the hard news to him, about Nexus, and let him know we were coming for him
		 tomorrow.
		-We asked him to sneak out and link up with Blade's troops (and Yflea) in the hills.
	-The third day, then, we indeed went to retrieve Silent Onyx and co.
		-During the flight, Sparrow, Blade's young companion, received an Infallible Messenger,
		 which spoke in a strange voice, calling him "Azada" and saying something about "The
		 Fivescore Fellowship" being recalled.
			-We've all heard the term: it's used for the secret masters of The Cult of the Illuminated,
			 presumably a reference to the Sidereals.
		-Then, with a strange look on his face, Sparrow began to perform a ritual, suddenly opening
		 some kind of gateway, and disappearing through it before any of us could reach him.
		-I reprimanded Blade for "picking up strays", but he disclaimed responsibility, saying he
		 _tried_ to get rid of him. . .
	-Completing the journey and finding our people, I greeted Silent Onyx.
		-"Ah, you weren't spared all the excitement, up in that cell, after all!"
			-There was a battlefield nearby, still being picked over by scavengers. He said he'd
			 witnessed a battle between a Marukani legion and undead here.
		-He told us that he'd witnessed the horselord arrested by a group of Marukani soldiers.
			-Presumably from that same legion.
			-A large group of bandits were also marched into town, and he and they were then all
			 executed.
		-I asked him if he thought Kerala's family was safe here. He was fairly sure the matter of
		 the bandits and the official's corruption were the cause of the executions, making the
		 situation here a fair bit better than it was, and certainly better than the crisis in Nexus.
	-We then returned to Nexus, arriving during the night of the third day PN (Post Nexus).
		-Still no sign of Rishi.
	-A few hours after landing, we could see a purple light, emanating from the center of the
	 ruined city, periodically flickering, but moving towards the encampment.
		-That does fit the anima of one of a Sidereal we once saw among The Cult, though we did
		 not rember them well (hmm. . .).
		-Eventually, from the city, emerged. . . Sparrow, crawling on his hands and knees, and
		 bleeding from many wounds.
			-The rest of the circle and I ran to. . . her? She was the spitting image of Sparrow,
			 but appeared to be a woman in her thirties, though, still short.
				-I paused only momementarily, and then went back to work with the compresses I'd
				 had Yflea make.
				-Her wounds were grim and various, cuts, fist-blows, many different weapons.
			-"They're. . . they're going to kill us all," she said.
			 "What?!?"
			 "The elders called us, said they wanted to talk about a treaty, now that The Empress
			  has returned. It was a trap. They have. . . something. . . like demons? Like the
			  Exalted, though, too? With animas. . .
			  It wasn't a peace talk. It was a massacre. I don't think Ayesha, any of the others
			  made it. . .
			  I had to use the last of this. . . Here, I don't think I'll be needing it any
			  longer. . ."
			 -At this last, she dropped another spell-storing cord, and fell unconscious.
				-I grabbed that once we were joined by more skilled medics, bugs and Solar cultists,
				 to take over for me.
	-We then sought out the Emissary, and asked her questions about Denandsor.
		-She claimed to know how to disable the defensive systems, but warned that some may have been
		 "damaged".
		-She claimed also that it has been untouched since Master Bax built the city, and was
		 doubtlessly filled with stores.
		-"I hated each of who you once were. There's no shame in admitting that. You were monsters.
		  I don't see those same people in you."
			-Aw, shucks.
		-She also pointed out that, if "Azada" is any indication, The Cult is now leaderless. . .
			-"They'll last without support for a time. But they can only destroy, not build. . ."
		-Libak also waved Ses's tongue about for a bit, asking what the hell this thing was.
			-It seemed to be an artifact, but a strange one, reminiscent of the worms that serve
			 the demon Kimberry, the Sea That Marched Against the Flame.
		-After that, though, Libak also did his damnedest to cheer up The Emissary, kind sould that
		 he is.
	-We indeed resolved to head to Denandsor with the refugees.
		-We worked towards the construction of ships, and, with funds from The Emissary, their
		 purchase, from less devestated communities upstream.
		-I spent my time with the sorcerers among The Cult, summoning more demons, eventually 
		 switching from bottle bugs to to puppeteers, to aid with the construction of ships, wagons,
		 and litters, for the journey to The Empty City.
			-The bugs flew through whatever alcohol we found, but the demons largely remained fairly
			 well behaved. The Emissary actually seemed to exert a calming effect on them, whenever

	-We spent two weeks in the area, getting this together.
		-During that time, many among the refugees began to publicly worship the Solars among them. . .
		-The Emissary seemed to be rather scornful of this practice, though she tried to hold her
		 tongue on the score, but occasionally slipped.
		-We also spoke with Azada.
			-She confessed that the purpose of The Cult was indeed to keep an eye on Solars, since
			 we're "dangerous".
				-I can't really argue with that last bit.
			-She also said that she stopped reporting on _us_, in particular, a while back, saying
			 she trusted us.
				-She seems young for the Sidereals, mentioning she Exalted a mere 300 years ago.
			-She spoke further about the massacre, saying she saw elders slaying one another, and
			 what she was sure was the detonation of a "Spirit Bomb".
				-The fight among elder Sidereals seemed to disturb her most, as she said that, "Not
				 even during The Ursurpation did it come to violence between the _Sidereals_.
			-She also mentioned that, "No one appears to be manipulating Fate at the moment."
				-That would seem to imply grim things about how many Sidereals were slain.
				-We fell to discussing options for exploiting this vacuum, but she broke in saying
				 that it may not be possible, for the gates of Heaven were sealed by those that
				 attacked her gathering.
			-She had a warning too, saying that Denandsor had been kept empty for _a reason_.
				-There, she claimed, Kel Bax had created a "false loom", a mockery of the Loom of
				 Fate in Heaven.
					-He had been granted a moment to look at the real one in Heaven, and that turned
					 out to be enough.
			-She seemed despondant, at the (near total) loss of her kind.
				-Libak spoke, though, of the people who _still lived_, who _will_ live.
				-At the last, her eyes lit up. ". . . _they_ will live again. Their exaltations will
				 come again. And I can predict where!"
					-That was apparently how the Wyld Hunt pursued us.
					-To do so, though, required a loom.
						-Denandsor, again. . .
						-Though she did also say that an orrery, in a city far to the East, buried
						 in jungle, could also serve.
				-Finding the new incarnations of the dead Sidereals could be one route to control
				 over Fate.
		-We asked The Emissary who else knew she had access to Denandsor.
			-"Only my circle and yours, those who fled to the Inivisble Manse."
	-By a third week, ships were beginning to come together.
		-With immediate injuries now seen to, I began to fear disease. There are many thousands of
		 refugees here, in temporary housing with limited infrastructure, and _more_ are actually
		 coming, as people from the many surrounding communities that were also devestated sought
		 out aid and leadership.
			-As such, I had a hard conversation with Yflea.
				-Since returning here with us, he'd been doing all he could to help people, using
				 his considerable medical and alchemical talents, and I let him know that there was
				 a way he could do more, but one with a cost. . . one that would bind him even
				 tighter to me, and change him.
				-Yflea had become a true believer. I think I got something across to him, for he
				 considered the matter for several hours, but then he came to me, asking to be
				 transformed.
				 "I can help the people still more, entrusted with this power, and I am already
				  yours in every way I can give. We will show the people the promise of the Shining
				  Ones fulfilled!"
				-And thus I took a day to cast Imbue Amalgam.
		-Pip also asked us who the people should be rallying around.
			-We debated us, each other, and their new city, but settled on The Unconquered Sun.
			-Along with that, we decided to promote protecting one another, and preparedness, as
			 great virtues.
				-Regardless of where things go from here, these people would soon be facing many
				 enemies.
			-Lesley's write up of this all: https://discord.com/channels/785604556934742036/785604557518405654/948059633820528700
			-Pip then saw to a campaign to infuence the people gathering around us, implementing
			 those goals, "to prevent another disaster like this from happening again."
	-With the ships together, we were able to make the journey down river inside of another week,
	 disembarking at the closest poin to Denandsor along the Grey River.
	-From there, we journeyed across savanahs and fields of tall grass.
		-Several times, we had to scare off or slay large predators, attracted by the column of
		 people, including one memorable incident in which Golden Blade had to go chase off a
		 tyrant lizard.
		-As we neared the city, wild life grew scarcer, and plants more scarce.
		-Eventually, we could see the city's skyline, glinting gold on the horizon.
		-Approaching, though, we felt a strange dread.
	-The column stopped and set up camp ten miles from the city.
		-Pip's work seemed to be paying off. We were greeted warmly where ever we went and Blade's
		 military drills saw ever escalating attendance.
		-We also heard prayers to The Unconquered Sun, perhaps more than had been offered to him
		 since The First Age.
	-Silent Onyx and Atraxian worked together to identify an approach through the city's outer
	 defenses, and scouted ahead.
		-They reported back that the city's robotic workforce was still maintaining the city, but
		 also that there was some strange activity going on, what Atraxian thought may be a
		 "resonance" between two of the city's different systems. The result was a confusion of
		 thoughts, and the feeling of dread we'd felt.
		-She said, and indeed we'd felt, that the the dread waxed and waned. It seemed strongest
		 at dusk, and weakest just before dawn.
		-She proposed an expedition at dawn, attempting to reach the city's control room, in it's
		 central spire.
		-Blade asked her about the details of the robots seen, and she indicated that many were
		 indeed built for combat.
		-Well, I then asked her if she knew how to bypass these defenses.
			-"The city will examine your essence, allowing in those that have been granted access.
			  Certain Solars were given this, along with a family of Dragonblooded, for whom it
			  would have been heritable."
			 "And do _you_ have this access?"
			 "Yes, as do you, given by Kel Bax to your previous incarnations."
	-As dawn came, we mounted our expedition into the city.
		-Most of it, we left to our allies from The Cult, many of then well suited to stealthy
		 intrusions.
		-They were able to shut down the defenses, and the field, and we began to explore the city.
	-We set the refugees up in a district of the city, within buildings that put even Nexus's finest
	 to shame.
		-The neighborhood even features a hydroponic farm, already filled with automatically harvested
		 food, restocked and recycled over and over again across the millenia since people dwelled here.
	-There remain unexplored districts of the city, though, areas Atraxian warned us were dangerous.
		-Military bunkers or the like, which could potentially be of use, but which may have guardians
		 unknown to her.
	-With us now somewhat settled, I suggested we get eyes on the surrounding landscape, and do what
	 we can to conceal signs of our passage to the city.
		-We set our allied Solars to the task, many of them being skilled in stealth and survival.
		-There's only so much that can be done to disguise the passage of many thousands, but we did
		 what we could.
	-We also began to see further refugees wandering the land.
		-We opted to invite in those who came, and to even reach out, carefully, to groups of
		 displaced people further afield.
			-We have more than enough room and supplies, and they need our help.
		-In talking with them, we heard various rumors.
			-The Marukani are at war, not just with Thorns but maybe also with The Realm.
			-_Something_ happened at Thorns, as refugees are coming from there too. Silent Onyx
			 recalled seeing a great light, off in that direction, while "captive".
			-Refugees were coming from the East too. They report a disaster in Chaya, where a flower
			 causing insanity is blooming out of season, instead of only once per year.
	-As Azada regained her strength, she attempted to work with Fate.
		-She worked a blessing for our circle (see your bio in Roll20).
		-She also worked a blessing over Denandsor and it's (new) people too, seeking their prosperity.
	-With the people settled, though, we began to turn our eyes to the exploration of the more
	 dangerous districts.

3/14/22:
	-Options for further city exploring:
		-The armory, capable of the automated production of arms and armor.
		-The more general Factory-Cathedral, producing the day to day goods of The Old Realm,
		 many even magical.
	-I suggested our choice should depend on our need, and asked Golden Blade and Libak what they
	 knew of our people's situation and that of the surrounding lands.
		-Golden Blades spies and scouts report:
			-The Realm is indeed on the move, and in conflict with Lookshy.
			-The Marukani are at war with. . . someone.
			-Something happened at Thorns, and now rogue ghosts and undead roam the surrounding,
			 marauding.
			-Nexus is ruined, but the automatons I awoke to protect it continue to do so. However,
			 we've heard reports that a Wyld zone within the city was growing and spreading. . .
			-In Great Forks, many people were displaced by the water, and now have formed bandit
			 gangs.
			-In the East, in Chaya, flowers causing insanity are blooming out of season.
			-The Hundred Kingdoms are embroiled in an especially intense civil war, the worst in
			 400 years.
		-Libak meanwhile reported that our quarters were also providing us food and water through
		 the still-functioning machinery, and that he and his family have been able to see to the
		 rest of their basic needs. However, there are few luxuries.
		-Well, walls without out guards stuffed with luxuries seems like a dangerous temptation. The
		 armory it is, then.
	-With the armory our chosen target, we then consulted with The Emissary, and what records we've
	 found in the city thus far, looking for details about the area.
		-The armory is a network of six Factory-Cathedrals, capable of producing sufficient arms for
		 a legion in a day.
		-To take control of the area, we'd need to infiltrate a control room in the central manse,
		 shutting down the larger weapon systems defending the area, including armies of automatons.
		-That will leave backup systems, like redundant generators, more independent automatons,
		 and such.
		-We learned some specifics about the guards of our target too, likely to include things like
		 lightning ballistas, warstriders piloted by automata, and still worse.
			-Golden Blade suggested a distraction of some kind, and wondered at the intelligence of
			 these automated defenses.
			-I replied that such machinery was often controlled by bound Little Gods, so they are
			 indeed intelligent and reactive.
	-Traveling to the area, Libak suggested a building to visit nearby, some place his past self had
	 commissioned. . . something, that was never delivered.
		-He led us to a great pool of some kind of oil. "Cooling oil", he referred to it as, saying
		 that the device likely remained there, submerged in the oil.
		-Blade and I looked at one another, both seemingly a bit unsure of getting in the oil, but
		 Libak (literally) dived right in.
		-While he fooled around down there, Blade and I began to hear the sound of metal on stone,
		 growing closer, which turned out to be a pack of metal, wolf-like automatons.
		-They raced over to us, lunging and biting at Golden Blade, who was nearest. I was quick to
		 the fray too, though only Blade managed to land a blow.
		-The oil, though, then began to roil. . .
		-What emerged was a red warstrider, apparently piloted by Libak, since it reached out and
		 swiped one of the wolves.
		-Wolves were soon dropping like flies, as each of the three of us claim at least one kill.
		-During the fray, Silent Onyx snuck away, his distraction apparently in hand.
	-Those wolf-things sorted, Golden Blade and I clambered aboard Libak's new warstrider, and we
	 went looking for more trouble, to provide Silent Onyx more cover.
		-Approaching the well guarded street before the shielded control chamber, we got the attention
		 of a large, low-to-the-ground war machine and the warstrider behind it.
		-I lept off Libak's warstrider, onto a nearby building, and his red warstrider surged forward,
		 slamming the war machine with it's arms and whip-like tail-blade.
		-Golden Blade kept riding a while longer, leaping _forward_ from one machine, onto the
		 low guardian machine. There, he struck it again and again with his sword, until something
		 cracked, releasing smoke, and the machine went still.
		-The enemy warstrider spent this time unlimbering an axe-like weapon but, before it could
		 step forward, Libak and his warstrider lept over wreckage and Blade both, running at it's
		 counterpart and punching it with a fist.
		-It responded with an axe blow that thankfully missed.
		-Undeterred by the size of his oponent, Golden Blade ran forward to the warstrider too,
		 hacking away at it's legs with his admittedly almost as oversized sword.
		-Over his head, Libak continued battering away at their opponent too.
		-I then lept onto the enemy warstrider, from the building I'd been running along, tearing
		 away at it's paneling with my wooden claws, until finally I reached, and destroyed, the
		 equally mechanical pilot within.
		-Libak and Golden Blade then ran by me, as I rode the failing warstrider to the ground, each
		 attacking one of the two lightening ballistas in the fortified square ahead.
		-I raced forward too, engaging two mechanical men at the front of the shield dome, raking
		 each with a clawed hand.
		-A few more swipes finished that job, while Golden Blade yelled about more wolves on their
		 way.
		-This continued for some time, us against various armored security assets, when some kind
		 of combat aircraft joined the fun, blasting the area with some sort of explosive weapon,
		 which thankfully all three of us managed to avoid the blast radius of.
		-Libak rushed to engage it in his warstrider, swinging at the aircraft that only he was
		 tall enough to reach.
		-Fortunately, before he'd managed to land more than one blow, the shield around the central
		 building went down, most of the automatons went still, and the aircraft flew off.
		-Looks like Silent Onyx was successful in reaching the control room!
		-From there, I set to examining the machinery all around us, identifying functions and
		 taking notes.
	-The armory's Factory-Cathedrals are also atelier manses, capable of being set to automatically
	 produce various things.
		-They can produce anything in Wonders of the Lost Age dealing with war.
	-All that military equipment, then, made taking the rest of the city trivial, and it is now fully
	 under our control.
	-We'll be having a month of downtime before our next session.
	-After that month, reports came in about Thorns, saying The Empress used the Sword of Creation.
		-In doing so, the Shadowlands in the area were sealed.
		-The being known as the Juggernaut, a huge undead creature with a city on it's back, was
		 destroyed, and lay rotting.
		-The Mask of Winters, his citadel / war beast destroyed, also somehow lost control of his
		 undead, and retreated back to The Underworld.
		-During the last week of that month, the corpse of the Juggernaut burst, unleashing a
		 torrent of horse-sized maggots. They're cutting a path of destruction through the land,
		 and are seemingly leading here. . .
